What Becomes Halal After Stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba
Ruling on what is permitted after stoning the Jamrat al-Aqaba on Yawm al-Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what becomes halal after stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, explain the hadith proof, and distinguish the exception for marital relations.

Core Idea
After stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, all ihram prohibitions lift except sexual intercourse until Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri: after the pilgrim performs the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba on Yawm al-Nahr, most restrictions of ihram are removed. The text provides a hadith from Ibn Abbas that confirms the general permission with a single explicit exception. We will unpack the dalil and its implications for the pilgrim's state.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice. The ruling is that after this, everything becomes halal except women (i.e., marital relations).
This is a gradual release from ihram prohibitions.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas narrated in Sunan Ibn Majah: 'When you have stoned the Jamrah, then everything becomes halal for you except women.'
The hadith is ahad, so its transmission is zanni but its meaning is clear.
3
Determine the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses a general phrase 'kullu shay' (everything) followed by an explicit exception 'illa al-nisa'. This indicates that all other prohibitions are lifted, and only marital relations remain prohibited.
The exception proves the rule: all other things are permitted.
4
Note the exception and its significance
The exception is women, i.e., sexual intercourse with one's spouse. The pilgrim must still perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah to make intercourse halal. Other acts like perfume, sewn clothes, and hunting become halal immediately.
This is based on the apparent meaning of the hadith and the Prophet's own practice.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab nuance
Some Shafi'i scholars restrict perfume until after shaving. The Hanafi school rejects this based on the general permission and the Prophet's use of musk after rami.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the framework of ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ حَلَّ لَهُ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءَ. وَجْه (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: «إِذَا رَمَيْتُمُ الْجُمْرَةَ، فَقَدْ حَلَّ لَكُمْ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا النِّسَاءَ» فَقَالَ لَهُ رَجُلٌ: يَا ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ وَالطَّيِّبُ؟ فَقَالَ: «أَمَّا أَنَا، فَقَدْ رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُضَمِّحُ رَأْسَهُ بِالْمِسْكِ، أَفَطِيبٌ ذَلِكَ، أَمْ لَا»( سنن ابن ماجة ، بَابُ مَا يَحِلُّ لِلرَّجُل، إِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ، رقم 3041) أصول: احناف کے نزدیک دسویں ذی الحجہ کو رمی جمار کرنے کے بعد جنسی خواہش کے علاوہ سب حلال ہے۔
And everything becomes halal for him except women. Aspect (1) the hadith for proof: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'When you have stoned the Jamrah, then everything becomes halal for you except women.' A man said to him: O Ibn Abbas, and perfume? He said: 'As for me, I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) anointing his head with musk, is that perfume or not?' (Sunan Ibn Majah, Chapter on what becomes halal for a man when he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba, no. 3041) Principle: According to the Hanafis, after stoning the jamarat on the tenth of Dhul Hijjah, everything except sexual desire is halal.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri: after a pilgrim stoning the Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah), everything becomes lawful for him except women (i.e., sexual relations with his spouse). The commentator then provides a hadith proof from Ibn Abbas, where the Companion explicitly states this ruling. When asked about perfume, Ibn Abbas indicates that perfume is permitted, citing the Prophet's own practice of applying musk after stoning. The Urdu usul note confirms that according to the Hanafi school, hunting, perfume, trimming nails, etc., are all permissible after rami; only marital relations remain prohibited until after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Key Terms
رَمْيُ الْجِمَارِ (ramy al-jimar): Stoning the pillars (jamarat) which is a rite of Hajj.
الْحَلَالُ (al-halal): That which is legally permissible (halal) after the prohibition of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba on Yawm al-Nahr, which of the following remains prohibited?
A) Wearing sewn clothes
B) Applying perfume
C) Sexual intercourse with one's spouse
D) Trimming nails

Key Takeaway
After stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, the pilgrim may resume all normal activities except marital relations, which remain prohibited until Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Timing and Conditional Raml/Sa'i
Rulings on performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah and conditions for raml and sa'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and explain the conditions under which raml and sa'i are performed during it.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is wajib on the 10th-12th of Dhul Hijjah; raml and sa'i depend on whether sa'i was already done after Tawaf al-Qudum.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents the ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the obligatory circumambulation of Hajj. It specifies its permissible days and sets out a conditional rule: if the pilgrim already performed Sa'i after the arrival tawaf, then no raml or sa'i is needed in this tawaf; otherwise, both are required. The author also cites hadith evidence for the timing and for the principle that Sa'i is not repeated. Understanding this ruling is crucial for performing Hajj correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation and timing
Read the first line: the pilgrim performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah on the day of Nahr or the next two days. This is the wajib tawaf of Hajj, consisting of seven circuits.
Note that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
2
Apply the conditional rule for raml and sa'i
The text gives two cases: if Sa'i was already done after Tawaf al-Qudum, then no raml and no sa'i in this tawaf. If not, then raml is performed and sa'i follows.
Raml is the quick walking with shoulder movement, sunnah in certain tawafs.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
Three hadith are cited: from Jabir (the Prophet went to the House on the day of Nahr and prayed Zuhr in Makkah), from Ibn Umar (the Prophet performed Tawaf on the day of Nahr), and from Jabir that Sa'i is not repeated. These support the timing and the rule on sa'i.
The hadith on non-repetition of Sa'i is key.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab perspective
The Hanafi school grades Tawaf al-Ziyarah as wajib, while Shafi'i and Maliki consider it a rukn. This affects the consequence of omission: in Hanafi, omission requires a dam (sacrifice); in other schools, Hajj is invalid.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يَأْتِي مَكَّةَ مِنْ يَوْمِهِ ذَلِكَ أَوْ مِنْ الْغَدِ أَوْ مِنْ بَعْدِ الْغَدِ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ طَوَافَ الزِّيَارَةِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطِ. فَإِنْ كَانَ سَعَى بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ عَقِيبَ طَوَافِ الْقُدُومِ لَمَّ يَرْمُلْ فِي هَذَا الطَّوَافِ وَلَا سَعْيَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَدَّمَ السَّعْيَ رَمَلَ فِي هَذَا الطَّوَافِ وَسَعَى بَعْدَهُ عَلَى مَا قَدَّمْنَا. وَجْه (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الله، . . . ثُمَّ رَكِبَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَأَفَاضَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ، فَصَلَّى بِمَكَّةَ الظُّهْرَ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1218/) وَجْه (۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ نَافِعٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم «أَفَاضَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ثُمَّ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ مِنِّى يَعْنِي رَاجِعًا» (أبو داؤد: بَابُ الْإِفَاضَةِ فِي الْحَجِّ، رقم: 1998) وَجْه (٤) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: سَمِعَ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، يَقُولُ: «لَمْ يَطْفِ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَلَا أَصْحَابُهُ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ إِلَّا طَوَافًا وَاحِدًا» (مسلم: بَابُ بَيَانِ أَنَّ السَّعْيَ لَا يُكَرَّرُ، نمبر: 1279)
Then he comes to Makkah on that day or the next day or the day after, and performs Tawaf of the Visit (Tawaf al-Ziyarah) seven circuits. If he performed Sa'i between Safa and Marwah immediately after the Tawaf of Arrival, he does not do Raml in this Tawaf and there is no Sa'i upon him. If he did not do Sa'i earlier, he does Raml in this Tawaf and performs Sa'i after it as we have mentioned. Aspect (2) the hadith for proof: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) rode and went to the House (Kaaba) and prayed Zuhr in Makkah (Muslim, Chapter on the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218). Aspect (2) the hadith for proof: from Nafi', from Ibn Umar, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) went out on the day of Nahr [for Tawaf], then prayed Zuhr in Mina returning (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Ifadah in Hajj, no. 1998). Aspect (4) the hadith for proof: I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah say: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions did not perform Tawaf between Safa and Marwah except one Tawaf' (Muslim, Chapter explaining that Sa'i is not repeated, no. 1279).
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah). The pilgrim may perform it on the day of Nahr (10th), the next day (11th), or the day after (12th). This is the obligatory tawaf of Hajj. It consists of seven circuits. The text then addresses the issue of Raml (quick walking with shoulder movement) and Sa'i. If the pilgrim had already performed Sa'i between Safa and Marwah after the Tawaf of Arrival (Qudum), then in this Tawaf he does not do Raml, and no Sa'i follows because it has already been done. However, if he did not perform Sa'i earlier, then he does Raml in this Tawaf and performs Sa'i after it, as previously explained in the chapter on Tawaf. The hadith proofs support the timing of Tawaf al-Ziyarah on the day of Nahr (from Jabir and Ibn Umar) and the principle that Sa'i is not repeated (from Jabir).

Key Terms
طَوَافُ الزِّيَارَةِ (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after stoning on Yawm al-Nahr, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
الرَّمَلُ (ar-ramal): Walking quickly with short steps and moving the shoulders, done in the first three circuits of certain tawafs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim performed Sa'i after Tawaf al-Qudum, what is required in Tawaf al-Ziyarah?
A) He must do Raml and Sa'i
B) He must do Raml but no Sa'i
C) He does not do Raml and no Sa'i
D) He does not do Raml but must do Sa'i

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is wajib and can be performed on 10th-12th; raml and sa'i depend on whether sa'i was done earlier.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah: The Obligatory Circumambulation
Ruling that after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, women become halal and this tawaf is the obligatory one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory tawaf of Hajj and explain the proof from Quran 22:29 and the practice of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory tawaf; after it, marital relations become permissible.

After completing the major rites of Hajj, the pilgrim performs a specific circumambulation known as Tawaf al-Ziyarah (or Tawaf al-Ifadah). This passage clarifies that this tawaf is the obligatory one, and it is the act that permits women (meaning marital relations) after the state of ihram. The author supports this with both the statement of the Companion Abdullah ibn Umar and a direct Qur'anic command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Tawaf al-Ziyarah; ruling: it is the prescribed (obligatory) tawaf of Hajj.
The text explicitly calls it 'al-mafrud'.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: the statement of Abdullah ibn Umar about staying in Mina, and the Quranic verse 22:29.
Ibn Umar's statement is a qawl al-sahabi, considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the verse: the imperative 'walyattawwafu' indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul. For Ibn Umar: his practice demonstrates the obligation to complete tawaf.
The hadith shows that if sunset catches the pilgrim in Mina on the middle day of Tashriq, he must stay to stone the next day, indicating that departure requires completion of all rites including tawaf.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
All schools agree on its obligation, but there is a dispute whether it is a rukn (pillar) or wajib (obligatory but not a pillar). The Shafi'i and Maliki schools consider it a rukn; the Hanafi school's relied-upon view also considers it a rukn.
A minority Hanafi view considers it wajib, but the majority and the text's wording favor rukn.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text calls it 'al-mafrud', which in Hanafi usage typically means fard (obligatory) and is understood as a rukn. The mufta bihi position is that it is a rukn; its omission invalidates the Hajj.
If omitted intentionally, Hajj is not valid; if missed unintentionally, it must be made up with a dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدْ حَلَّ لَهُ النِّسَاءُ وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ هُوَ الْمَفْرُوضُ فِي الْحَجّ. وَجْه (٥) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ: عَبْدَ اللهِ بْنَ عُمَرَ كَانَ يَقُولُ: " مَنْ غَرَبَتْ عَلَيْهِ الشَّمْسُ وَهُوَ عِنّى مِنْ أَوْسَطِ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ فَلَا يَنْفِرَنَّ حَتَّى يَرْمِيَ الْجِمَارَ مِنَ الْغَدِ * (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ مَنْ غَرَبَتْ لَهُ الشَّمْسُ يَوْمَ النَّفْرِ الْأَوَّلِ مِنِّى أَقَامَ حَتَّى يَرْمِيَ الْجِمَارَ يَوْمَ الثَّالِثِ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ، نمبر: 9646) وَجْه (٥) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ: ثُمَّ لْيَقْضُوا تَفَثَهُمْ وَلْيُوفُوا نُذُورَهُمْ وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ (سورة الحج، 22، الآية نمبر: 29)
And women become halal for him, and this Tawaf is the prescribed (obligatory) one in Hajj. Aspect (5) the statement of the Companion for proof: Abdullah ibn Umar used to say: 'Whoever the sun sets upon while he is in Mina on the middle of the days of Tashriq, he should not depart until he stones the Jamarat the next day.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on one whom the sun sets on the first day of departure from Mina... no. 9646) Aspect (5) the verse for proof: 'Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and circumambulate the Ancient House.' (Surah al-Hajj 22:29)
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage concludes the ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah: after performing it, marital relations become permissible (complete tahallul). This tawaf is the fard (obligatory) tawaf of Hajj; any other tawaf is sunnah or nafl. The commentator brings two proofs: (1) The statement of Ibn Umar that a pilgrim who stays in Mina until sunset on the middle day of Tashriq must stay to stone the next day. This indirectly shows that after completing all rites including tawaf, one may depart. (2) The Qur'anic verse (22:29) which commands circumambulation of the Kaaba after completing rites (tafath and nudhur). The verse is understood to refer to Tawaf al-Ifadah.

Key Terms
الْمَفْرُوضُ (al-mafrud): The obligatory act; in this context, Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory tawaf of Hajj.
تَفَثُهُمْ (tafathuhum): The remaining state of ihram including untrimmed nails, hair, etc.; 'completing their rites'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when do women (marital relations) become halal for the pilgrim?
A) After stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba
B) After shaving the head
C) After Tawaf al-Ziyarah
D) After Sa'i

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is the obligatory circumambulation of Hajj, after which all ihram prohibitions are lifted.

Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Makruh and Dam Required
Ruling that delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond its days is makruh and requires a dam according to Abu Hanifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah and explain the proof from the companion's statement.

Core Idea
Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond its days requires a dam — even though the act itself is only makruh.

The timing of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is not a simple recommendation; the Hanafi school attaches a compensatory obligation (dam) if it is delayed beyond the prescribed days. This lesson examines the ruling and the proof from a companion's statement that any delay in Hajj rites incurs an expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is performed on the days of Nahr (10th–12th Dhul Hijjah). Delaying it is makruh; if delayed beyond these days, dam becomes wajib according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Understand the consequence of delay
If the pilgrim delays the tawaf beyond its prescribed days, a sacrificial animal (dam) is obligatory as compensation.
This is Abu Hanifa's view; the Sahibayn may differ.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the statement (qawl) of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever advances something of his Hajj or delays it, let him spill blood for that.'
Recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The general command 'falyuhriq daman' covers all forms of delay, including tawaf. Thus, delaying tawaf incurs a dam.
The companion's statement is considered a valid proof (qawl sahabi) in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ تَأْخِيرُهُ عَنْ هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ فَإِنْ أَخَرَهُ عَنْهَا لَزِمَهُ دَمٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ أَخَرَ الْخَلْقَ دِ [؟]. وَجْه (۱) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ: عَن ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «مَنْ قَدَّمَ شَيْئًا مِنْ حَجِّهِ أَوْ أَخَّرَهُ، فَلْيُهْرِقْ لِذَلِكَ دَمًا» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في الرَّجُلِ يَحْلِقُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ، نمبر: 14958) أصول: طواف زیارت کو ایا نحر سے زیادہ موخر کرنے سے دم لازم ہو گا، امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک۔
And it is disliked (makruh) to delay it (Tawaf al-Ziyarah) from these days. If he delays it beyond them, a dam is incumbent upon him according to Abu Hanifa. And likewise if he delays the shaving (of the head) ... Aspect (1) the statement of the Companion for proof: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'Whoever advances something of his Hajj or delays it, let him spill blood (i.e., sacrifice an animal) for that.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Chapter on a man shaving before slaughtering, no. 14958) Principle: Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the day of Nahr necessitates a dam according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond its prescribed days (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah). The matn states it is makruh (disliked) to delay it, but if one delays it entirely (i.e., postpones it until after the days of Tashriq), a dam (sacrificial animal) becomes wajib (obligatory) according to Abu Hanifa. The same applies if one delays the shaving of the head (halq) beyond its proper time. The proof is the statement (qawl) of Ibn Abbas that any advancement or delay of Hajj rites requires expiation (dam). The Urdu usul note summarizes: from Abu Hanifa's perspective, delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond Yawm al-Nahr necessitates a dam.

Key Terms
دَمٌ (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a goat or sheep) required as expiation for certain omissions in Hajj.
الْخَلْقُ (al-khalqu): The shaving of the head (halq) or trimming of hair, a rite of tahallul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The tawaf is invalid
B) He must repeat the Hajj
C) He must sacrifice a dam
D) No penalty, but it is makruh

Key Takeaway
Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the days of Nahr requires a dam as compensation according to Abu Hanifa, based on the general principle of the companion's statement.

Returning to Mina After Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Ruling that after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the pilgrim returns to Mina to stay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that returning to Mina after Tawaf al-Ziyarah is sunnah muakkadah and cite the two hadith proofs from Muslim and Abu Dawud.

Core Idea
Returning to Mina after Tawaf al-Ziyarah is sunnah, proven by the Prophet's practice of praying Zuhr there and spending the nights.

After completing Tawaf al-Ziyarah on the day of Nahr, the pilgrim is not required to stay in Makkah. The matn instructs: 'Then he returns to Mina and stays there.' This lesson examines the proof for this sunnah ruling, which is based on the direct practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is returning to Mina and staying there after Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended).
Not wajib; omission does not invalidate the hajj.
2
Locate the first hadith (Muslim)
The hadith from Muslim (no. 1308) reports that the Prophet performed Tawaf al-Ifadah on the day of Nahr, then returned to Mina and prayed Zuhr there.
This establishes the act of returning to Mina.
3
Locate the second hadith (Abu Dawud)
The hadith from Abu Dawud (no. 1958) reports that when asked about spending the night in Makkah, Ibn Umar stated that the Prophet spent the nights in Mina and remained there.
This emphasizes staying overnight in Mina during the days of Tashriq.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Both hadiths show the Prophet's actual practice (fi'l). In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's fi'l indicates recommendation (sunnah) unless there is additional evidence for obligation.
Since no command is given, the ruling remains sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then he returns to Mina and stays there. He said: 'As for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), he spent the night in Mina and remained there.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on spending the night in Makkah during the nights of Mina, no. 1958)

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that after performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the pilgrim returns to Mina and stays there for the days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th). This is the sunnah of the Prophet. Two hadiths are cited: (1) The Prophet performed Tawaf al-Ifadah on the day of Nahr and then returned to Mina for Zuhr prayer. (2) When asked about staying in Makkah during the nights of Mina, Ibn Umar stated that the Prophet spent the nights in Mina, not in Makkah. This establishes that it is sunnah to stay in Mina during the days of Tashriq.

Key Terms
مِنًى (Mina): A valley near Makkah where pilgrims stay during the days of Tashriq after returning from Arafat.
أَيَّامُ التَّشْرِيقِ (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following Yawm al-Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah).

Timing of Rami on the 11th of Dhul Hijjah
Ruling on timing of rami on the 11th

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for stoning the three jamarat on the 11th and identify the proofs from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Stoning on the 11th begins after zawal (sun's decline).

This lesson covers the ruling on the timing of rami on the second day of Nahr (11th Dhul Hijjah). The Hanafi school holds that the pilgrim must wait until after zawal (past noon) to stone the three jamarat, beginning with the one nearest the mosque. Two proofs from the Prophet’s practice and the Companion Ibn Umar reinforce this sunnah timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time
The act is rami of three jamarat on 11th Dhul Hijjah. The prescribed time is after zawal.
Zawal is the sun's decline from its zenith.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs: (1) Ibn Umar's statement that they waited for zawal (Bukhari). (2) Aisha's description of the Prophet stoning after Zuhr (Abu Dawud).
Both are ahad hadith.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Both indicate that the Prophet and Companions only stoned after the sun declined, establishing this as the sunnah time.
4
Note the ruling consequence
Stoning before zawal is makruh but valid; after zawal is sunnah and more virtuous.
Mufta bihi: after zawal is the preferred time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ زَالَتْ الشَّمْسُ مِنْ الْيَوْمِ الثَّانِي مِنْ النَّحْرِ رَمَى الْجِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ يَبْتَدِئُ بِالَّتِي تَلِي الْمَسْجِدَ. وَجْه (۱) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ: سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، مَتَى أَرْمِي الْجِمَارَ؟ قَالَ: «إِذَا رَمَى إِمَامُكَ، فَارْمِهْ» فَأَعَدْتُ عَلَيْهِ الْمَسْأَلَةَ، قَالَ: «كُنَّا نَتَحَيَّنُ فَإِذَا زَالَتِ الشَّمْسُ رَمَيْنَا» (بخاري بَابُ رَمْيِ الْجِمَارِ، نمبر: 1746) وَجْه (۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، قَالَتْ: «أَفَاضَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنْ آخِرٍ يَوْمِهِ حِينَ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَى مِنًى، فَمَكَثَ بِمِنًى لَيَالِي أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ يَرْمِي الْجِمَارَ، إِذَا زَالَتِ الشَّمْسُ كُلُّ جَمْرَةٍ بِسَبْع حَصَيَاتٍ، يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ، وَيَقِفُ عِنْدَ الْأُولَى، وَالثَّانِيَةِ فَيُطِيلُ الْقِيَامَ، وَيَتَضَرَّعُ، وَيَرْمِي الثَّالِثَةَ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا» (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي رَمْيِ الْجِمَارِ، نمبر: 1973) أصول: دسویں ذی الحجہ کو جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی اور گیارہویں ذی الحجہ کو تینوں جمرات کی رمی کرے۔
And when the sun declines from the zenith on the second day of Nahr (i.e., 11th Dhul Hijjah), he stones the three Jamarat, beginning with the one nearest the mosque (i.e., the first jamrah). Aspect (1) the statement of the Companion for proof: I asked Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them), 'When do I stone the Jamarat?' He said: 'When your Imam stones, then stone.' I repeated the question to him, he said: 'We used to wait, and when the sun declined (zawal), we stoned.' (Bukhari, Chapter on stoning the Jamarat, no. 1746) Aspect (2) the hadith for proof: from Aisha, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went out (for tawaf) at the end of his day when he prayed Zuhr, then he returned to Mina and stayed in Mina during the nights of the days of Tashriq, stoning the Jamarat when the sun declined, each Jamrah with seven pebbles, saying Allahu Akbar with each pebble, and he stood at the first and second (jamrah) prolonging the standing and supplicating, and he stoned the third (jamrah) and did not stand at it.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on stoning the Jamarat, no. 1973) Principle: On the tenth of Dhul Hijjah, one stones Jamrat al-Aqaba, and on the eleventh, one stones all three Jamarat.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for stoning on the second day of Nahr, i.e., 11th Dhul Hijjah (first day of Tashriq). The pilgrim must wait until after zawal (past noon) when the sun has declined from its zenith. He then stones the three Jamarat in order, starting with the Jamrah closest to the Masjid (i.e., the first jamrah near Masjid al-Khayf), then the middle, then Jamrat al-Aqaba. The proofs: (1) Ibn Umar told the questioner that they would wait for zawal to stone, as per the practice. (2) Aisha describes the Prophet's practice of stoning after Zuhr, with seven pebbles per jamrah, making takbir, and standing for supplication at the first two jamarat. The Urdu usul note summarizes the sunnah: on the 10th, only Jamrat al-Aqaba is stoned; on the 11th, all three jamarat are stoned.

Key Terms
الزَّوَالُ (az-zawal): The sun's decline from its zenith; the beginning of the time for Zuhr prayer.
الْجَمْرَةُ الثَّالِثَةُ (al-jamrah ath-thalithah): The third and farthest jamrah, also called Jamrat al-Aqaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At any time before Zuhr
B) After Fajr
C) After the sun passes the zenith (zawal)
D) Only at night

Key Takeaway
The sunnah for rami on the 11th (and 12th) is to begin after the sun declines from the zenith.

Ruling on Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah
States ruling and condition with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah and identify the required compensation according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the days of Tashriq obligates a dam; the delay itself is merely makruh.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hajj: what happens if a pilgrim delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah (the essential circumambulation) beyond its established time – the days of Tashriq (11th-13th Dhul-Hijjah). The matn of Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi position that while the delay is disliked (makruh), it triggers a wajib compensation: a dam (sacrifice). We will walk through the ruling, its condition, and the evidence from hadith that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default time
Tawaf al-Ziyarah (Tawaf al-Ifadah) is a wajib part of Hajj. Its preferred time is the day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah) or the days of Tashriq (11-13th). The matn states it is disliked to delay beyond these days.
The days of Tashriq are the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul-Hijjah.
2
State the consequence of delay
If the pilgrim delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the days of Tashriq, a dam (blood offering) becomes obligatory. This is the view of Abu Hanifa, as per the matn.
Note: The delay itself is makruh tanzihi (disliked), not haram.
3
Locate the proof
The commentary provides two hadith proofs: first, a general hadith from Ibn Abbas that whoever advances or delays anything in Hajj must shed blood; second, hadith from Ibn Umar showing the Prophet's practice of returning to Mina after Tawaf.
The hadith are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Sahih Muslim.
4
Analyze the legal implication
The command 'falyuhriq daman' indicates wujub (obligation) because, in Hanafi usul, the imperative form (amr) implies obligation unless there is a contrary indicator. The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but sufficient for wajib rulings.
The ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

It is disliked to delay it beyond these days. If he delays it beyond them, a dam (blood offering) is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, if he delays the creation? Then he returns to Mina and stays there. (Proofs: Hadith of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar). Urdu: Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the day of Nahr necessitates a dam according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the matn of Al-Quduri, with additional hadith citations. The matn states that it is makruh (disliked) to delay Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the days of Tashriq (11th-13th Dhul-Hijjah). If one delays it beyond those days, he must offer a dam (sacrifice of a sheep) as compensation. This is the view of Abu Hanifa. The commentary then provides two proofs: First, a hadith from Ibn Abbas (reported by Ibn Abi Shayba) that whoever advances or delays anything of his Hajj should shed blood. Second, a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet performed Tawaf al-Ifadah on the day of Nahr and then returned to Mina. Another narration indicates that the Prophet stayed in Mina during the nights of Tashriq. The Urdu summary clarifies that this ruling applies to Tawaf al-Ziyarah and that the dam is required when delayed beyond the day of Nahr.

Key Terms
تَأْخِيرُهُ (ta'khiruhu): Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the days of Tashriq (11-13 Dhul-Hijjah).
دَم (dam): A blood offering (sacrifice of a sheep or equivalent) required as compensation for certain violations in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is still valid with no penalty.
B) A dam (blood offering) is required according to Abu Hanifa.
C) The Hajj becomes invalid.
D) He must repeat the Tawaf.

Key Takeaway
Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah beyond the days of Tashriq obligates a dam (blood offering) according to Abu Hanifa, and the delay itself is disliked but not invalidating.

Stoning the Jamarat on the Days of Tashriq: Timing and Method
Details the timing and method of stoning the three Jamarat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing and method of stoning the three Jamarat on each day of Tashriq and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Stoning must be after zawal; stand for dua at first two jamarat but not at Aqabah.

This passage from al-Quduri details the wajib acts of stoning during the Days of Tashriq. Correct timing and method are essential for a valid Hajj. The text presents the ruling and supports it with the practice of the Prophet and his Companions, providing a clear guide for the pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the days of stoning
Determine which days of Dhul-Hijjah require stoning: the 11th, 12th, and optionally the 13th if staying.
The 10th (Yawm al-Nahr) only requires stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah.
2
Note the prescribed time
Stoning must begin after zawal (sun's decline past the meridian) on each day.
This is based on the hadith 'kunnā nataḥayyanu fa-idhā zālat al-shamsu ramaynā'.
3
Describe the method for each jamrah
Each jamrah is stoned with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each throw. The order is: first the nearest to Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle, then Jamrat al-Aqabah.
4
Distinguish standing after stoning
After the first two jamarat, one stands facing the qibla and makes lengthy supplication. After Jamrat al-Aqabah, one does not stand but departs.
This is based on the hadith of Aisha: 'yaqifu 'inda al-ūlā wa al-thāniyati ... wa lā yaqifu 'indahā'.
5
Understand the option to hasten
After stoning on the 12th, the pilgrim may leave for Makkah (nafar) or stay and stone again on the 13th.
Staying until the 13th is considered better (afdal).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ زَالَتْ الشَّمْسُ مِنْ الْيَوْمِ الثَّانِي مِنْ النَّحْرِ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ يَبْتَدِئُ بِالَّتِي تَلِي الْمَسْجِدَ د . وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ زَالَتْ الشَّمْسُ مِنْ الْيَوْمِ الثَّانِي سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، مَتَى أَرْمِي الْحِمَارَ؟ قَالَ: «إِذَا رَمَى إِمَامُكَ، فَارْمِهْ» فَأَعَدْتُ عَلَيْهِ الْمَسْأَلَةَ، قَالَ: «كُنَّا نَتَحَيَّنُ فَإِذَا زَالَتِ الشَّمْسُ رَمَيْنَا» (بخاري بَابُ رَمْيِ الْحِمَارِ، نمبر: 1746) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ زَالَتْ الشَّمْسُ مِنْ الْيَوْمِ الثَّانِي اعَنْ عَائِشَةَ، قَالَتْ: «أَفَاضَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنْ آخِرٍ يَوْمِهِ حِينَ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَى مِنْ، فَمَكَثَ بِمَا لَيَالِي أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ يَرْمِي الجُمْرَةَ، إِذَا زَالَتِ الشَّمْسُ كُلُّ جَمْرَةٍ بِسَبْع حَصَيَاتٍ، يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ، وَيَقِفُ عِنْدَ الْأُولَى، وَالثَّانِيَةِ فَيُطِيلُ الْقِيَامَ، وَيَتَضَرَّعُ، وَيَرْمِي الثَّالِثَةَ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا» (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي رَمْيِ الْحِمَارِ، نمبر: 1973) اصول : دسویں ذی الحجہ کو جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی اور گیارہویں ذی الحجہ کو تینوں جمرات کی رمی کرے۔  فَيَرْمِيهَا بِسَبْع حَصَيَاتٍ يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلّ حَصَاةٍ وَيَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا فَيَدْعُو ثُمَّ يَرْمِي الَّتِي تَلِيهَا مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ وَيَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا ثُمَّ يَرْمِي جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ كَذَلِكَ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا ٢٠ فَإِذَا كَانَ مِنْ الْغَدِ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ كَذَلِكَ الفَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَتَعَجَّلَ النَّفْرَ نَفَرَ إِلَى مَكَّةَ وَإِنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يُقِيمَ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ فِي الْيَوْمِ الرَّابِعِ بَعْدَ زَوَالِ الشَّمْسِ رَضِيَ وَه وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَيَرْمِيهَا بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَرْمِي الْجُمْرَةَ الدُّنْيَا بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ، يُكَبِّرُ عَلَى إِثْرِ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ، ثُمَّ يَتَقَدَّمُ حَتَّى يُسْهِلَ، فَيَقُومَ مُسْتَقْبِلَ القِبْلَةِ، فَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، وَيَدْعُو وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ، ثُمَّ يَرْمِي الوُسْطَى ثُمَّ يَأْخُذُ ذَاتَ الشِّمَالِ فَيَسْتَهِلْ، وَيَقُومُ مُسْتَقْبِلَ القِبْلَةِ، فَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، وَيَدْعُو وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ، وَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، ثُمَّ يَرْمِي جَمْرَةَ ذَاتِ العَقَبَةِ مِنْ بَطْنِ الوَادِي، وَلاَ يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا، ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُ، فَيَقُولُ «هَكَذَا رَأَيْتُ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَفْعَلُهُ» (بخاري بَابُ إِذَا رَمَى الجُمْرَتَيْنِ، يَقُومُ وَيُسْهِلُ: 1751) 10 وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا كَانَ مِنْ الْغَدِ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، مَتَى أَرْمِي الحِمَارَ؟ قَالَ: «إِذَا رَمَى إِمَامُكَ، فَارْمِهِ» فَأَعَدْتُ عَلَيْهِ الْمَسْأَلَةَ، قَالَ: كُنَّا نَتَحَيَّنُ فَإِذَا زَالَتِ الشَّمْسُ رَمَيْنَا» (بخاري بَابُ رَمْيِ الْحِمَارِ، نمبر: 1746) رَضِيَ وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا كَانَ مِنْ الْغَدِ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، قَالَتْ: «أَفَاضَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنْ آخِرِ يَوْمِهِ حِينَ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَى مِنِّي، فَمَكَثَ بِمَا لَيَالِيَ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ يَرْمِي الْجُمْرَةَ، إِذَا زَالَتِ الشَّمْسُ كُلُّ جَمْرَةٍ بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ، يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ، وَيَقِفُ عِنْدَ الْأُولَى، وَالثَّانِيَةِ فَيُطِيلُ الْقِيَامَ، وَيَتَضَرَّعُ، وَيَرْمِي الثَّالِثَةَ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا» (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ في رمي الجمار، نمبر 1973) الا وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَتَعَجَّلَ النَّفْرَ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ يَعْمَرَ الدِّيلِي، قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَهُوَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَجَاءَ نَاسٌ أَوْ نَفَرٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ نَجْدٍ فَأَمَرُوا رَجُلًا فَنَادَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَيْفَ الْحَجُ؟ ، فَأَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ رَجُلًا فَنَادَى «الْحَجُّ الْحَجُ ، يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ، مَنْ جَاءَ قَبْلَ صَلَاةِ الصُّبْحِ مِنْ لَيْلَةِ جَمْع فَتَمَّ حَبُّهُ (ابو داؤد: بَابُ مَنْ لَمْ يُدْرِكْ عَرَفَةَ، نمبر : 1949 الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أَدْرَكَ الْإِمَامَ بِجَمْعِ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الحج، غمبر (889)
When the sun declines on the second day of Nahr (11th), he stones the three jamarat, beginning with the one nearest the mosque. (Proofs: hadith of Ibn Umar and Aisha about stoning after noon). Urdu: On the 10th, stone Jamrat al-Aqabah; on the 11th, stone all three. He stones each with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each, and stands at the first two making dua, then stones Jamrat al-Aqabah similarly without standing. Then on the next day (12th), he stones the three after noon similarly. If he wishes to hasten departure, he leaves for Makkah; if he wishes to stay, he stones the three on the fourth day (13th) after noon. (Proofs: hadith of Ibn Umar and Aisha on stoning after noon, and hadith of Abdur Rahman bin Ya'mar on the essence of Hajj).
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage details the ruling on stoning the Jamarat during the Days of Tashriq. The matn states that on the second day of Nahr (11th Dhul-Hijjah), after the sun has passed its zenith (zawal), the pilgrim stones the three jamarat in order: first the one nearest to the Masjid al-Khayf (the small jamrah), then the middle, then Jamrat al-Aqabah. For each jamrah, seven pebbles are thrown with takbir. After the first two, one stands facing the qibla and makes lengthy supplication, but no standing at the third. The same procedure is followed on the third day (12th) after noon. If the pilgrim wishes to hasten departure (nifr), he may leave for Makkah on the 12th after stoning; if he stays, he must stone the three on the fourth day (13th) as well. The commentary provides multiple hadith proofs: the practice of Ibn Umar, the hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's actions, and the hadith of Ibn Ya'mar defining the core of Hajj. The Urdu summary emphasizes the sequence of stoning on 10th and 11th.

Key Terms
رَمَى الْجَمْرَةَ (rama al-jamrah): To pelt the designated stone pillars (jamarat) with seven small pebbles.
نَفَرَ (nafara): To depart from Mina to Makkah after completing the stoning; hastening (ta'jil) on the 12th is allowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding standing after stoning the first two jamarat?
A) One must stand at all three.
B) One must stand at the first two for lengthy dua, but not at Jamrat al-Aqabah.
C) Standing is not required at any.
D) Only the Imam stands.

Key Takeaway
Stoning the jamarat must be performed after noon on each day of Tashriq, and standing for dua after the first two jamarat is a Sunnah practice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Manner and Timing of Stoning the Jamarat
Stating the procedure for stoning the three jamarat on the days of Tashriq with proofs from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for stoning the jamarat, identify the required actions and correct timing, and justify the ruling using the hadith proofs provided.

Core Idea
Stone each jamarah with seven pebbles, saying takbir each time; stand and supplicate after the first two, but not after Jamrat al-Aqaba.

This lesson explains the exact manner and timing of stoning the three jamarat during Hajj, as established by the Hanafi school. Based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and his companions, the rules ensure that this wajib ritual is performed correctly. You will learn the sequence, the importance of standing for supplication, and the time restrictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that stoning the jamarat is a wajib action in the Hanafi school. Note the three jamarat: al-Ula, al-Wusta, and Jamrat al-Aqaba.
The number of pebbles is seven for each jamarah.
2
Note the manner for each
After stoning the first two, the pilgrim stands, faces the qibla, and makes lengthy supplication. After Jamrat al-Aqaba, he does not stand.
This difference is evident in the hadith of Ibn Umar.
3
Recognize the timing
On the day of Nahr (10th), stoning can be from dawn to sunset. On the 11th and 12th, it must be after noon. The option of nafr (hastening) allows departure after the 12th if stoning is completed.
The hadith from Aisha specifies stoning after zuhr.
4
Locate the proofs
The hadith from Ibn Umar (Bukhari 1751) details the manner, and from Aisha (Abu Dawud 1973) confirms the timing. These serve as the basis for the Hanafi ruling.
The Hanafi school treats these actions as wajib based on the Prophet's consistent practice.

فَيَرْمِيهَا بِسَبْع حَصَيَاتٍ يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلّ حَصَاةٍ وَيَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا فَيَدْعُو ثُمَّ يَرْمِي الَّتِي تَلِيهَا مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ وَيَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا ثُمَّ يَرْمِي جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ كَذَلِكَ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا وَفَإِذَا كَانَ مِنْ الْغَدِ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ كَذَلِكَ فَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَتَعَجَّلَ النَّفْرَ نَفَرَ إِلَى مَكَّةَ وَإِنْ أَرَادَ أَنْ يُقِيمَ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ فِي الْيَوْمِ الرَّابِعِ بَعْدَ زَوَالِ الشَّمْسِ. وه وجه: (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَيَرْمِيهَا بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَرْمِي الْجُمْرَةَ الدُّنْيَا بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ، يُكَبِّرُ عَلَى إِثْرِ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ، ثُمَّ يَتَقَدَّمُ حَتَّى يُسْهِلَ، فَيَقُومَ مُسْتَقْبِلَ القِبْلَةِ، فَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، وَيَدْعُو وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ، ثُمَّ يَرْمِي الوُسْطَى ثُمَّ يَأْخُذُ ذَاتَ الشِّمَالِ فَيَسْتَهِلْ، وَيَقُومُ مُسْتَقْبِلَ القِبْلَةِ، فَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، وَيَدْعُو وَيَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ، وَيَقُومُ طَوِيلًا، ثُمَّ يَرْمِي جَمْرَةَ ذَاتِ العَقَبَةِ مِنْ بَطْنِ الوَادِي، وَلاَ يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا، ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُ، فَيَقُولُ: «هَكَذَا رَأَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَفْعَلُهُ» (بخاري: بَابُ إِذَا رَمَى الجُمْرَتَيْنِ، يَقُومُ وَيُسْهِلُ: 1751). وجه: (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا كَانَ مِنْ الْغَدِ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، مَتَى أَرْمِي الحِمَارَ؟ قَالَ: «إِذَا رَمَى إِمَامُكَ، فَارْمِهُ» فَأَعَدْتُ عَلَيْهِ الْمَسْأَلَةَ، قَالَ: كُنَّا نَتَحَيَّنُ فَإِذَا زَالَتِ الشَّمْسُ رَمَيْنَا» (بخاري: بَابُ رَمْيِ الْحِمَارِ، نمبر: 1746). وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا كَانَ مِنْ الْغَدِ رَمَى الْحِمَارَ الثَّلَاثَ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، قَالَتْ: «أَفَاضَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِنْ آخِرِ يَوْمِهِ حِينَ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَى مِنِّي، فَمَكَثَ بِمَا لَيَالِيَ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ يَرْمِي الْجُمْرَةَ، إِذَا زَالَتِ الشَّمْسُ كُلُّ جَمْرَةٍ بِسَبْعِ حَصَيَاتٍ، يُكَبِّرُ مَعَ كُلِّ حَصَاةٍ، وَيَقِفُ عِنْدَ الْأُولَى، وَالثَّانِيَةِ فَيُطِيلُ الْقِيَامَ، وَيَتَضَرَّعُ، وَيَرْمِي الثَّالِثَةَ وَلَا يَقِفُ عِنْدَهَا» (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ في رمي الجمار، نمبر: 1973). الا وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَتَعَجَّلَ النَّفْرَ عَنْ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ يَعْمَرَ الدِّيلِي، قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَهُوَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَجَاءَ نَاسٌ أَوْ نَفَرٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ نَجْدٍ فَأَمَرُوا رَجُلًا فَنَادَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَيْفَ الْحَجُ؟ فَأَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ رَجُلًا فَنَادَى: «الْحَجُّ الْحَجُّ، يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ، مَنْ جَاءَ قَبْلَ صَلَاةِ الصُّبْحِ مِنْ لَيْلَةِ جَمْعٍ فَقَدْ تَمَّ حَجُّهُ» (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَنْ لَمْ يُدْرِكْ عَرَفَةَ، نمبر: 1949، الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أَدْرَكَ الْإِمَامَ بِجَمْعٍ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الحَجَّ، نمبر: 889).
He stones them with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each pebble, and stands at it supplicating. Then he stones the next one similarly and stands at it. Then he stones Jamrat al-Aqaba likewise, but does not stand at it. Then when it is the next day, he stones the three jamarat after noon similarly. Then if he wants to hasten, he departs to Makkah; if he wants to stay, he stones the three jamarat on the fourth day after sunset. And that is a face: (1) the statement of a Companion for proof ... [the hadith texts follow]
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting the manner and timing of stoning the jamarat during Hajj. The base text from Al-Quduri describes the procedure: on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), the pilgrim stones the three jamarat—first the small (al-jamrat al-ula), then the middle (al-wusta), and finally Jamrat al-Aqaba—with seven pebbles each, saying takbir with each pebble. After the first two, he stands facing the qibla and makes lengthy supplication; for Jamrat al-Aqaba, he does not stand. On the following day (11th), he stones all three again after noon. If he wishes to hasten (an yata'ajjal al-nafr), he may depart to Makkah after stoning on the 12th; otherwise, he stays and stones again on the 13th (the fourth day) after noon. The commentary then provides hadith proofs: Ibn Umar's practice narrated by Bukhari (1751) shows the exact manner; another hadith from Ibn Umar (Bukhari 1746) confirms stoning after noon; Aisha's hadith (Abu Dawud 1973) adds that the Prophet prayed zuhr first then stoned; and a hadith from Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'mar (Abu Dawud 1949, Tirmidhi 889) defines Hajj and the timing for haste. The Hanafi ruling is that stoning the jamarat is wajib, and the time for stoning on the 11th and 12th begins after zuhr (zawal). The exception for timing on the day of Nahr is that it can be done from dawn to sunset, but the sunnah is to do it after sunrise.

Key Terms
رَمْيُ الْجِمَارِ (Ramy al-Jimār): The act of throwing pebbles at the stone pillars in Mina during Hajj.
جَمْرَةُ الْعَقَبَةِ (Jamrat al-ʿAqaba): The largest pillar, nearest to Makkah, stoned on the day of Nahr and subsequent days.
النَّفْرُ (al-Nafr): Departure from Mina after completing the stoning; hastening (nafr awwal) on the second day (12th) or staying (nafr thani) until the third day (13th).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many pebbles does the pilgrim throw at each jamarat on the day of Nahr?
A) Seven, with takbir at each
B) Three, with takbir only at the first
C) Seven, without takbir
D) Five, with takbir at each

Key Takeaway
Stoning the jamarat is a wajib ritual performed with seven pebbles at each pillar, accompanied by takbir, with standing for supplication after the first two, and timing after noon on the days of Tashriq (except day of Nahr).

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Stoning Before Noon (11th Dhul Hijjah)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of stoning on the second day of tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn on stoning before noon on the second day, and explain the evidence each side uses.

Core Idea
Stoning before noon on 11th Dhul Hijjah is valid according to Abu Hanifa but not according to the Sahibayn; the latter is the mufta bihi.

This passage records an intra-Hanafi disagreement over the permissible time for stoning on the second day of Mina (11th Dhul Hijjah). While all agree that stoning is an obligatory rite, they differ on whether it can be performed before noon. The matn gives the core ruling, and the commentary supplies proofs from hadith and the statement of a Companion. Understanding this dispute clarifies how later Hanafi practice settled on requiring stoning after noon on the days following the day of Nahr.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the ruling attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa: stoning on this day is permissible before noon, after dawn.
This is the view recorded in the matn as 'jaza'.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's objection
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold it is not permissible before noon. Their view is the mufta bihi (operative position) in the school.
They are referred to as 'wa qala' (they said) in the text.
3
Follow the first proof: statement of Ibn Abbas
Examine the qawl sahabi cited: when the forenoon expands on the day of the second nafr, stoning becomes forbidden. This supports the Sahibayn's restriction.
The commentary adds a related hadith from Bayhaqi about staying until after noon if the sun sets on the first nafr.
4
Follow the second proof: hadith of Jabir
Analyze the hadith: the Prophet stoned on the day of Nahr before noon, but for the following days he stoned after noon. This distinction is key.
Abu Hanifa uses analogy from the day of Nahr; the Sahibayn restrict the exception to that day only.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: if a pilgrim stones before noon on 11th, Abu Hanifa considers it valid; the Sahibayn require repetition after noon. The later school adopts the Sahibayn's view.
Tarjih by Al-Marghinani and others: the hadith explicitly limits permission to the day of Nahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢ فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الرَّمْيَ فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ جَازَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَا يَجُوزُ. وجه: (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الرَّمْيَ فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: إِذَا انْتَفَحَ النَّهَارُ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّفْرِ الْآخِرِ فَقَدْ حَرَّ الرَّمْيُ، وَالصَّدْرُ (سنن للبيهقي: مَنْ غَرَبَتْ لَهُ الشَّمْسُ يَوْمَ النَّفْرِ الْأَوَّلِ مِنًى أَقَامَ حَتَّى يَرْمِيَ الْحِمَارَ يَوْمَ الثَّالِثِ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ: 9687). وجه: (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الرَّمْيَ فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ جَابِرَ بْنَ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، يَقُولُ: «رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَرْمِي عَلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ضُحًى، فَأَمَّا بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَبَعْدَ زَوَالِ الشَّمْسِ» (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي رَمْيِ الْحِمَارِ، نمبر: 1971).
12: If he advances the stoning on this day before noon after dawn, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible. Face: (1) the statement of a Companion as proof for "if he advances the stoning on this day" from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, he said: "When the forenoon has expanded on the day of the second nafr, then stoning has become forbidden, and the chest" (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, section: On whom the sun sets on the first day of nafr in Mina, he stays until he stones the jamarat on the third day after noon: 9687). Face: (2) the hadith as proof for "if he advances the stoning on this day before noon" that he heard Jabir ibn Abdullah saying: "I saw the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, stoning on his mount on the day of Nahr in the forenoon. As for after that, it was after noon" (Abu Dawud, chapter on stoning the jamarat: 1971).
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the time for stoning on the second day (11th Dhul Hijjah). The base matn states that if a person performs the stoning on this day before noon (zawal) after dawn, it is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it is not permissible. The commentary then provides two proofs: first, a statement of Ibn Abbas (a Companion's opinion) that when the forenoon expands, the time for stoning becomes restricted, implying that stoning is only allowed after noon. Second, a hadith from Jabir that the Prophet stoned on the day of Nahr in the forenoon, but for the following days he stoned after noon. This hadith is used by Abu Hanifa to argue that stoning before noon on the first day is permissible by analogy, but the Sahibayn restrict the permissibility only to the day of Nahr and require after noon for subsequent days. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position among the Hanafis is that stoning on the 11th and 12th must be after noon; early stoning is not valid without a valid reason. The authority_weight: the ruling in the matn is from Zahir al-Riwayah, and the dispute is well-known.

Key Terms
الزَّوَال (al-Zawāl): The moment when the sun passes its zenith, i.e., noon; the start of zuhr time.
النَّفْرُ الْآخِر (al-Nafr al-Ākhir): The final departure from Mina on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of stoning on the second day (11th) before noon according to the two Sahibayn?
A) Permissible
B) Not permissible
C) Mandatory
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Stoning on the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah must be performed after noon (zawal) according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, based on the hadith of Jabir.

Ruling on Sending Baggage Ahead to Makkah
Stating the ruling that it is disliked to send one's baggage ahead to Makkah while staying in Mina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending baggage ahead to Makkah while staying in Mina and explain the proof from Umar's statement.

Core Idea
Sending baggage ahead to Makkah during Hajj while staying in Mina is disliked, not forbidden.

This lesson addresses a specific etiquette of Hajj: whether a pilgrim may send his heavy baggage to Makkah while he remains in Mina to complete the stoning. The Hanafi school rules this act as makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked), based on a strong statement from Umar ibn al-Khattab. Understanding the precise ruling and its proof prevents both overreaction and neglect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the Arabic text 'yukrahu an yuqaddima al-insan thaqalahu ila Makkah'. What is the act? What ruling does 'yukrahu' convey in Hanafi fiqh?
The act is sending one's heavy baggage to Makkah while staying in Mina. 'Yukrahu' indicates makruh tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited).
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a statement of Umar: 'Whoever sends his baggage on the night he departs, there is no Hajj for him.' Identify the source and type of this proof.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi (Companion's statement) from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah. Its transmission (thubut) is zanni.
3
Interpret the proof
Umar's literal words seem to nullify Hajj. How do Hanafi scholars interpret this? Why do they not take it literally?
The severe expression is understood as hyperbolic discouragement (tashdid) to emphasize the disliked nature, not actual nullification. The essential acts (arkan) of Hajj remain valid.
4
Apply the ruling
If a pilgrim sends his baggage after completing the stoning, does the ruling apply? Why or why not?
The ruling specifically applies when one stays in Mina to complete the stoning. After stoning, the reason for dislike ceases, so sending baggage is no longer disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يُقَدِّمَ الْإِنْسَانُ ثَقَلَهُ إِلَى مَكَّةَ وَيُقِيمَ حَتَّى يَرْمِيَ ١٣. وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يُقَدِمَ الْإِنْسَانُ ثَقَلَهُ إِلَى مَكَّةَ قَالَ عُمَرُ: «مَنْ قَدَّمَ ثِقَلَهُ لَيْلَةَ يَنْفِرُ فَلَا حَجَّ لَهُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: مَنْ كَرِهَ أَنْ يُقَدِّمَ ثِقَلَهُ مِنْ مِنًى: 15389).
And it is disliked that a man sends his baggage ahead to Makkah while he stays until he stones. Face (1): the statement of a Companion as proof for "and it is disliked that a man sends his baggage ahead to Makkah" that Umar said: "Whoever sends his baggage on the night he departs, there is no Hajj for him" (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: section on who disliked sending his baggage from Mina: 15389).
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on the etiquette of Hajj: it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) for a pilgrim to send his heavy baggage to Makkah while he remains behind in Mina to complete the stoning. The proof cited is a statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) which strongly condemns such an action, saying that whoever sends his baggage on the night he intends to depart, his Hajj is incomplete. However, the Hanafi scholars interpret this as a severe warning indicating dislike (karahah) rather than complete invalidation, because the essential acts of Hajj (stoning, tawaf, etc.) remain unaffected. The ruling applies specifically to the days of Tashriq when one is required to stay in Mina for the stoning. The authority_weight of this ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah as part of the matn of Al-Quduri.

Key Terms
الثَّقَل (al-Thaqal): Heavy baggage or belongings of the pilgrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible
B) Disliked
C) Forbidden
D) Required

Key Takeaway
Sending baggage ahead to Makkah while staying in Mina to complete the stoning is makruh tanzihi; the severe warning from Umar is interpreted as discouragement, not nullification.

Descent at al-Muhassab: A Sunnah of Hajj
Stating a sunnah of Hajj with a supporting hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on descending at al-Muhassab and explain why it is classified as sunnah muakkadah based on the prophetic action.

Core Idea
Descending at al-Muhassab is a sunnah, not wajib—the Prophet's action shows recommendation, not obligation.

When the pilgrim departs from Mina to Makkah for the tawaf al-ifadah or tawaf al-sadr, the Hanafi school recommends a brief stop at a place called al-Muhassab (also known as al-Abtah). This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, and clarifies that it is a recommended act, not an obligatory one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that when the pilgrim departs to Makkah, he descends at al-Muhassab. Determine whether this is an obligation or recommendation by examining the language and context.
The verb 'nazala' (descends) is used without a command, indicating a recommended practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites a hadith from Anas ibn Malik about the Prophet's actions at al-Muhassab. Identify the specific parts of the hadith that are relevant.
The hadith mentions praying four prayers and resting before proceeding to tawaf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the prophetic action proves the ruling. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's voluntary acts indicate desirability (istihbab) unless there is evidence to elevate it to obligation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it cannot establish an obligation, only a sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi school considers it sunnah muakkadah, some other scholars treat it as mere mustahabb. Understand that this is a valid difference within the scope of recommended acts.
The practical consequence is the same: it is encouraged but not required.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that it is sunnah muakkadah, meaning it is highly recommended and the Prophet consistently did it.
Omitting it is not sinful and does not require any compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا نَفَرَ إِلَى مَكَّةَ نَزَلَ بِالْمُحَصَّبِ ١٥. وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا نَفَرَ إِلَى مَكَّةَ نَزَلَ بِالْمُحَصَّبِ أَنَّ أَنَسَ بْنَ مَالِكٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، حَدَّثَهُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَّهُ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ وَالْعَصْرَ، وَالْمَغْرِبَ وَالعِشَاءَ، وَرَقَدَ رَقْدَةً بِالْمُحَصَّبِ، ثُمَّ رَكِبَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ، فَطَافَ بِهِ (بخاري: بَابُ مَنْ صَلَّى العَصْرَ يَوْمَ النَّفْرِ بِالأبْطَحِ، نمبر: 1764/ مسلم: بَابُ اسْتِحْبَابِ طَوَافِ الْإِفَاضَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ، نمبر: 1309).
Then when he departs to Makkah, he descends at al-Muhassab. Face: (1) the hadith as proof for "when he departs to Makkah, he descends at al-Muhassab", that Anas ibn Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, narrated from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he prayed Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha, and slept a sleep at al-Muhassab, then rode to the House and performed tawaf around it (Bukhari: chapter on who prayed Asr on the day of nafr at al-Abtah: 1764; Muslim: chapter on desirability of tawaf al-ifadah on the day of Nahr: 1309).
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on a recommended act (sunnah) when the pilgrim departs from Mina to Makkah for the tawaf al-ifadah or tawaf al-sadr. The matn states that he should descend (nazala) at al-Muhassab, which is a place between Mina and Makkah (also known as al-Abtah). The commentary brings a hadith from Anas that the Prophet performed prayers and rested there before entering Makkah for tawaf. According to the Hanafi school, this is a sunnah act, not wajib; if omitted, nothing is required. The phrase 'nazala' indicates a recommendation. The authority_weight: the ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الْمُحَصَّب (al-Muḥaṣṣab): A valley between Mina and Makkah, also called al-Abtah, where the Prophet rested before entering Makkah for tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Go directly to the Kaaba without stopping
B) Descend at al-Muhassab, pray, and rest
C) Stone the jamarat again
D) Shave or trim the hair

Key Takeaway
Descending at al-Muhassab is a sunnah muakkadah of Hajj; omitting it does not invalidate the Hajj nor require compensation, but following it earns reward.

Tawaf al-Sadr: Obligation and Proof
Ruling with dalil from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadr, identify its proof from hadith, and explain why the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for non-Makkans; the command in the hadith indicates obligation.

This lesson focuses on the ruling of Tawaf al-Sadr (the farewell circumambulation), a key rite at the conclusion of Hajj. The Hanafi school holds this tawaf to be wajib for pilgrims except those from Makkah. We will examine the matn statement and the dalil that supports it, understanding the legal reasoning behind the hukm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the matn: after descending at al-Muhassab, the pilgrim enters Makkah and performs seven circuits without raml. This is Tawaf al-Sadr. Note its ruling: 'wa huwa wajib illa ala ahli Makkah' (it is obligatory except for the people of Makkah).
The exemption is specific to residents of Makkah.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'The people were commanded that their last covenant be with the House, except that it was lightened for the menstruating woman' (Bukhari 1755). Identify this as a Sunnah ahad dalil.
The hadith is also narrated in another version with similar wording.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative word 'umira' (were commanded) is an imperative, which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah (context) to the contrary. The exception for menstruating women confirms that the command is generally binding, with a specific concession.
The Hanafi rule: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is that Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib; omission requires a dam (blood sacrifice). Some other schools consider it sunnah muakkadah. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
The thamarah al-khilaf: compensation due on omission.
5
Apply the ruling
A non-Makkan pilgrim who omits Tawaf al-Sadr must sacrifice a sheep (dam) as compensation. A Makkan pilgrim is not required to perform it at all.
If the omission is intentional or unintentional, the dam obligation remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يَدْخُلُ مَكَّةَ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ لَا يَرْمُلُ فِيهَا وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الصَّدَرِ ٢٦ وَهُوَ وَاجِبٌ إِلَّا عَلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ ثُمَّ يَعُودُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ. وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت ثُمَّ يَدْخُلُ مَكَّةَ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاس رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: «أُمِرَ النَّاسُ أَنْ يَكُونَ آخِرُ عَهْدِهِمْ بِالْبَيْتِ، إِلَّا أَنَّهُ خُفِّفَ عَن الحَائِضِ» (بخاري: بَابُ طَوافِ الوَدَاعِ، نمبر: 1755). ل وجه: (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَهُوَ وَاجِبٌ إِلَّا عَلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ، قَالَ: كَانَ النَّاسُ يَنْصَرِفُونَ فِي كُلِ وَجْهِ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا يَنْفِرَنَّ أَحَدٌ حَتَّى يَكُونَ آخِرُ عَهْدِهِ بِالْبَيْتِ» ثُمَّ يَعُودُ. اصل: جب حاجی غیر اہل مکہ ہو تو منی سے مکہ پہونچے تو طواف وداع کرے، یہ واجبی امر ہے۔
Then he enters Makkah and performs tawaf around the Kaaba seven circuits without walking quickly in it, and this tawaf is Tawaf al-Sadr, and it is obligatory except for the people of Makkah. Then he returns to his family. Face (1): the statement of a Companion as proof for that he enters Makkah and performs tawaf around the Kaaba seven circuits: from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, he said: "The people were commanded that their last covenant be with the House, except that it was lightened for the menstruating woman" (Bukhari: chapter on tawaf al-wada': 1755). For a face: (1) the hadith as proof for that it is obligatory except for the people of Makkah: from Ibn Abbas, he said: "The people were departing in every direction, so the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Let no one depart until his last covenant is with the House.'" Then he returns. Principle: When a pilgrim is not from the people of Makkah and arrives from Mina to Makkah, he should perform the farewell tawaf; this is an obligatory matter.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on Tawaf al-Sadr (also called Tawaf al-Wada', the farewell circumambulation). The matn states: after descending at al-Muhassab, the pilgrim enters Makkah and performs seven circuits around the Kaaba without raml (quick pace with short steps), and this tawaf is called Tawaf al-Sadr. It is wajib (obligatory) except for the residents of Makkah. Then the pilgrim returns to his homeland. The commentary provides two proofs: first, Ibn Abbas reports that people were commanded to make the House their last connection, except for menstruating women (Bukhari 1755). Second, another hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said no one should depart until his last action is tawaf of the House. The Urdu summary clarifies that for non-Makkans, this tawaf is wajib. The Hanafi school rules that Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib; omitting it requires a dam (blood sacrifice). The exemption for Makkans is because they are residents and do not leave with the intention of returning home from a journey. The authority_weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
طَوَافُ الصَّدَرِ (Ṭawāf al-Ṣadr): The farewell circumambulation performed after completing all Hajj rites before leaving Makkah.
الرَّمَل (al-Ramal): Walking quickly with short steps in the first three circuits of tawaf; not performed in Tawaf al-Sadr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All women
B) People of Makkah
C) People who performed Hajj in a previous year
D) Men only

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib for non-Makkan pilgrims; its omission requires a dam, but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Stoning Before Noon on the Day of Nahr: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of ramy on the day of Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on stoning before noon on the day of Nahr and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits stoning before noon on the day of Nahr; the Sahibayn require after noon.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi disagreement concerning the timing of the stoning (ramy) on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). While all agree on the obligation of ramy, they differ on when it may be performed. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to navigate multiple valid opinions within the school and apply the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the day
The act is ramy (stoning) of the Jamrat al-Aqaba on the day of Nahr. Note that this is a distinct ruling: for other days of Tashreeq, timing is after zawal by consensus.
The day of Nahr has special flexibility according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the three positions
Abu Hanifa: valid after dawn (fajr). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: invalid before zawal. Note that both agree that the earliest time after dawn is contested.
The Sahibayn's view aligns with the common practice of the Prophet as reported in sound hadith.
3
Understand the basis of difference (inferred)
Although the source does not cite proofs, the difference stems from how each imam interprets the general permission to begin Hajj rites at dawn vs. the specific Prophetic practice of stoning after noon. Abu Hanifa extends the concession to ease for pilgrims; the Sahibayn prioritize the literal timing of the Sunnah.
This is a classic example of ra'y (reasoning) vs. riwayah (transmission) within the Hanafi school.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is more flexible and follows the principle of taysir (facilitation).
Later Hanafi authorities like al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah adopt this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الرَّمْيَ فِي هَذَا الْيَوْمِ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ جَازَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَا يَجُوزُ
If he performs the stoning on this day before noon after dawn, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of the stoning (ramy) on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one performs the stoning after dawn but before noon (zawal), it is valid. However, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani), hold that stoning before noon is not valid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the madhhab is the view of Abu Hanifa, as it is the most lenient and practical. This ruling applies specifically to the day of Nahr; for the other days of Tashreeq, the time for stoning begins after zawal by consensus.

Key Terms
الرَّمْي (ar-ramy): The stoning of the jamarat (pillars) during Hajj.
الزَّوَال (az-zawāl): The zenith of the sun, the moment it begins to decline from its highest point.
يَوْمُ النَّحْر (yawm an-nahr): The day of sacrifice, 10th Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is valid after dawn.
B) No, it is only valid after noon.
C) It is valid only after sunrise.
D) It depends on the intention.

Key Takeaway
On the day of Nahr, Abu Hanifa permits stoning from dawn, while his disciples require noon; the school follows Abu Hanifa for ease.

Dislike of Sending Luggage Ahead and Ruling on Tawaf al-Sadar
Rulings on post-ramy procedures and farewell tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on sending luggage ahead before ramy (makruh) and on tawaf al-sadar (wajib), and identify the exception for Makkans.

Core Idea
Sending luggage ahead disrupts Hajj sequence; farewell tawaf is wajib, not fard, and missing it demands a dam.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses two important post-ramy matters: the etiquette of moving one's belongings and the obligation of the farewell tawaf. The rulings are straightforward but carry significant consequences. Let's break them down step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first ruling
The text states that sending heavy luggage (thaqal) to Mecca before completing the stoning (ramy) is disliked (makruh). Understand that this ruling applies to someone who remains in Mina to perform the ramy and sends his belongings ahead.
The dislike is due to violating the proper order of rites.
2
Identify the second ruling and its obligation level
After leaving Mina, the pilgrim should stay at al-Muhassab (sunnah), then enter Mecca and perform tawaf of seven circuits without ramal. This is tawaf al-sadar (farewell tawaf). The text explicitly says it is wajib, except for the people of Mecca.
Wajib means obligatory; omission requires a dam (sacrifice). It is not fard (pillar).
3
Note the exception for Makkans
Makkans are exempt from tawaf al-sadar because they do not depart from Mecca as non-Makkans do. For non-Makkans, it is a final rite before returning home.
This exception is specific and textually stated.
4
Understand the consequence of omission
If a non-Makki pilgrim omits tawaf al-sadar, the Hajj is still valid (sahih) but a dam becomes wajib. This distinguishes it from a fard act, whose omission invalidates Hajj.
The dam is an additional sacrifice; consult a scholar for procedure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يُقَدِّمَ الْإِنْسَانُ ثَقَلَهُ إِلَى مَكَّةَ وَيُقِيمَ حَتَّى يَرْمِيَ فَإِذَا نَفَرَ إِلَى مَكَّةَ نَزَلَ بِالْمُحَصَّبِ ثُمَّ يَدْخُلُ مَكَّةَ فَيَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ لَا يَرْمُلُ فِيهَا وَهَذَا الطَّوَافُ طَوَافُ الصَّدَرِ وَهُوَ وَاجِبٌ إِلَّا عَلَى أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ ثُمَّ يَعُودُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ
And it is disliked for a person to send his heavy luggage to Mecca and stay (in Mina) until he performs the stoning. Then when he leaves (Mina) to Mecca, he stays at al-Muhassab, then enters Mecca and performs tawaf of the House seven circuits, without jogging (ramal) in them. And this tawaf is the tawaf of farewell (tawaf al-sadar), and it is wajib except for the people of Mecca. Then he returns to his family.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings. First, it is makruh (disliked) for a pilgrim to send his heavy baggage to Mecca ahead of time while he remains in Mina to complete the stoning. This is because the proper sequence of Hajj rituals includes remaining in Mina for the stoning. Second, when the pilgrim leaves Mina for Mecca, he should descend at al-Muhassab (a place between Mina and Mecca) as a sunnah practice. Upon entering Mecca, he performs tawaf al-sadar (farewell tawaf) of seven circuits without ramal (quick walking), which is a wajib act for non-Makkans; Makkans do not have to perform it because they do not depart from Mecca. After that, he may return to his family. The tawaf al-sadar is the final tawaf that concludes the Hajj.

Key Terms
الثَّقَل (ath-thaqal): Heavy luggage or belongings of the pilgrim.
طَوَاف الصَّدَر (tawāf as-sadar): The farewell tawaf performed after the final stoning before leaving Mecca.
الْمُحَصَّب (al-muḥaṣṣab): A place between Mina and Mecca where it is sunnah to stay briefly after leaving Mina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Sending luggage ahead before stoning is makruh; tawaf al-sadar is wajib for non-Makkans, and its omission requires a dam.

Saqt of Tawaf al-Qudum When Going Directly to Arafat
Ruling on tawaf al-qudum for a muhrim who bypasses Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tawaf al-qudum for a muhrim who bypasses Mecca and identify the consequence of its omission.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-qudum is sunnah; bypassing Mecca drops it with no penalty.

This short but decisive passage from the matn clarifies the status of tawaf al-qudum (the arrival tawaf) in the Hajj. Many pilgrims wonder whether they must perform this tawaf if they proceed directly to Arafat without entering Mecca. The text settles the matter: it is a recommended act (sunnah), and its omission in this scenario carries no financial or ritual penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under discussion
The act is tawaf al-qudum, the circumambulation performed upon first entering Mecca for Hajj.
It is distinct from tawaf al-ifadah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj).
2
Identify the conditional scenario
The scenario is that the muhrim does not enter Mecca at all but goes directly to Arafat for the wuquf.
This assumes the pilgrim arrives at a point outside Mecca (e.g., Jeddah) and heads straight to Arafat.
3
State the ruling
The ruling is that tawaf al-qudum is waived (saqat) from him. It is no longer required.
Saqt means the obligation or recommendation drops due to the absence of its basis.
4
State the consequence of omission
There is no penalty (la shay'a 'alayhi) for leaving it — no dam, no fidyah, no need to repeat.
This confirms that tawaf al-qudum is not wajib; if it were wajib, omission would require a dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْخُلْ الْمُحْرِمُ مَكَّةَ وَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى عَرَفَاتٍ وَوَقَفَ بِمَا عَلَى مَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ فَقَدْ سَقَطَ عَنْهُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ لِتَرْكِهِ
If the muhrim does not enter Mecca and goes to Arafat and stands there as we have previously described, then the tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) is waived from him, and there is no obligation upon him for leaving it.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage clarifies that tawaf al-qudum (the arrival tawaf) is not an independent obligation; it is sunnah according to the Hanafi school. If a muhrim bypasses Mecca and proceeds directly to Arafat for the standing, he does not have to come back to Mecca for tawaf al-qudum. No compensation (dam) is required. This is because the primary purpose of tawaf al-qudum is to honor the Kaaba upon entering Mecca, but if one does not enter Mecca, the basis for this tawaf is absent. The 'standing' (wuquf) at Arafat is the rukn of Hajj, and the pilgrim has fulfilled the essential obligation.

Key Terms
طَوَاف الْقُدُوم (tawāf al-qudūm): The tawaf performed upon first entering Mecca for Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of omitting tawaf al-qudum when one goes directly to Arafat without entering Mecca?
A) Must perform a dam
B) Must repeat the tawaf after Hajj
C) No penalty
D) Hajj is invalid

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah act; if the pilgrim does not enter Mecca, it is dropped entirely without any obligation.
