Time for Wuquf at Arafat and Validity for Unconscious Person
Rulings on the timing of wuquf and its sufficiency for those unaware

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time window for wuquf at Arafat and identify when a person's presence suffices even without awareness.

Core Idea
Wuquf at Arafat is the pillar of Hajj; mere presence within the defined time suffices, even if unaware.

This lesson covers the essential timing of the central rite of Hajj—the standing at Arafat. The text from Al-Quduri defines when this act is considered performed and clarifies that consciousness is not a condition for its validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that wuquf at Arafat is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj. If it is missed, Hajj is invalid.
2
Define the time window
Note that the time for wuquf begins at zawal (noon) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah (day of Arafah) and ends at fajr (dawn) of the 10th (day of Nahr).
3
Determine sufficiency conditions
Understand that mere presence within this time is enough. Even if a person is asleep, unconscious, or unaware of being in Arafat, the wuquf is valid.
The textual proof: 'And whoever passes through Arafat while he is asleep, or unconscious, or does not know that it is Arafat, that suffices.'
4
Note the implication
If a pilgrim catches any moment of the designated time, their Hajj is valid. No other conditions regarding awareness or intentional standing are mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَدْرَكَ الْوُقُوفَ بِعَرَفَةَ مَا بَيْنَ زَوَالِ الشَّمْسِ مِنْ يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ إِلَى طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الْحَجَّ وَمَنْ اجْتَازَ بِعَرَفَةَ وَهُوَ نَائِمٌ أَوْ مُغْمًى عَلَيْهِ أَوْ لَمْ يَعْلَمْ أَنَّهَا عَرَفَةُ أَجْزَاهُ ذَلِكَ عَنْ الْوُقُوفِ
And whoever catches the standing at Arafat between the noon of the day of Arafah and the dawn of the day of Nahr, then he has caught the Hajj. And whoever passes through Arafat while he is asleep, or unconscious, or does not know that it is Arafat, that suffices him for the standing.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage defines the time of wuquf (standing) at Arafat, which is the rukn (pillar) of Hajj. According to all schools, the time for wuquf begins at zawal (noon) on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah (day of Arafah) and extends until dawn (fajr) of the 10th (day of Nahr). If a person is present in Arafat at any point within this window, even if only momentarily, his Hajj is valid. The second ruling clarifies that consciousness or awareness is not a condition for the validity of wuquf. If a person passes through Arafat while asleep, unconscious (e.g., in a coma), or simply unaware that he is in Arafat, his wuquf is still considered valid. This is based on the principle that the reality of wuquf is presence in Arafat, and the intention is made at the time of ihram, so additional awareness at the moment of presence is not required.

Key Terms
الْوُقُوف (al-wuqūf): The standing or presence at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
يَوْمُ النَّحْر (yawm an-naḥr): The day of sacrifice, 10th Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sunset of the day of Arafah
B) Midnight of the 9th
C) Dawn (fajr) of the day of Nahr (10th)
D) Zawal of the 10th

Key Takeaway
Wuquf at Arafat is valid by mere presence within the specified time, regardless of awareness.

Ruling on Tawaf al-Qudoom and Time for Wuquf
Ruling on dropping Tawaf al-Qudoom and time for Wuquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on missing Tawaf al-Qudoom and identify the valid time for wuquf at Arafat.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Qudoom is sunnah; missing it incurs no penalty. Valid wuquf: from zawal on 9th to fajr on 10th.

This lesson clarifies two key rulings in Hajj: the status of Tawaf al-Qudoom and the time window for the essential standing at Arafat. Understanding these will help you avoid common misconceptions about what is obligatory and what is merely recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The first act discussed is Tawaf al-Qudoom. According to the text, if the muhrim does not enter Makkah and goes straight to Arafat, this tawaf drops and no penalty is required. This indicates that Tawaf al-Qudoom is not obligatory but a sunnah.
The text uses 'سقط' (dropped) and 'لا شيء عليه' (nothing upon him).
2
Identify the consequence of omission
Since it is sunnah, leaving it incurs no dam (penalty) and does not affect the validity of Hajj.
Contrast with wajib acts like Tawaf al-Ifadah which require a penalty if missed.
3
Identify the time for wuquf
The valid time for standing at Arafat begins at zawal (noon) on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah and ends at fajr (dawn) on the 10th. Anyone who stands within this period, even for a moment, has caught the Hajj.
Wuquf is the rukn (pillar) of Hajj; performing it within this time is essential.
4
Understand the implication
If a pilgrim catches the wuquf within this time, his Hajj is valid even if he missed Tawaf al-Qudoom or other sunnan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِن لَم يَدْخُلُ الْمُحْرِمُ مَكَّةَ وَتَوَجَّهَ إلَى عَرَفَاتِ وَوَقَفَ بِمَا عَلَى مَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ فَقَدْ سَقَطَ عَنْهُ طَوَافُ الْقُدُومِ وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ لِتَرْكِهِ. وَمَنْ أَدْرَكَ الْوُقُوفَ بِعَرَفَةَ مَا بَيْنَ زَوَالِ الشَّمْسِ مِنْ يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ إِلَى طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الْحَجَّ.
If the muhrim does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat and stands there as we have explained, then Tawaf al-Qudoom drops from him and there is nothing upon him for leaving it. And whoever catches the standing at Arafat between the noon of the day of Arafat and the dawn of the day of Nahr has caught the Hajj.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage contains two separate rulings. First, Tawaf al-Qudoom (circumambulation of arrival) is sunnah, not fard or wajib. If a pilgrim in ihram goes directly to Arafat without entering Makkah, this tawaf is dropped and no dam (penalty) is required. Second, the valid time for wuquf at Arafat extends from zawal (noon) on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah until fajr on the 10th. Anyone who stands within this time, even for a moment, has validly performed the Hajj. Both rulings are foundational in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (Tawaf al-Qudoom): The circumambulation of arrival performed by the muhrim upon entering Makkah.
الوقوف (al-wuquf): The standing at Arafat, the essential pillar of Hajj.
يوم النحر (Yawm an-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, the day of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudoom if a muhrim goes directly to Arafat without entering Makkah?
A) It must be performed later, otherwise Hajj is invalid.
B) It drops and no penalty is required.
C) It is wajib and a dam is required if missed.
D) It is fard and must be made up.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudoom is sunnah; missing it has no penalty. The valid time for wuquf at Arafat is from zawal on 9th to fajr on 10th.

Wuquf Without Consciousness: Physical Presence Suffices
Ruling on the validity of wuquf without consciousness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wuquf when the pilgrim is asleep, unconscious, or unaware, and identify the key condition for its validity.

Core Idea
Physical presence at Arafat suffices; consciousness is not required for wuquf.

Many assume that acts of worship require full awareness and intention. However, the Hanafi school rules that standing at Arafat (wuquf) is an exception: the pillar is physical presence within the boundaries during the prescribed time. In this lesson, we examine the explicit text from Al-Quduri that confirms this leniency, opening a window into how the Hanafi school prioritizes the letter of the ritual over mental states.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text addresses the act of 'passing by Arafat' (ijtaza bi Arafah) and declares it sufficient (ajzahu) for wuquf. Establish that the ruling is validity (sihha).
The ruling applies to the Hajj pillar of wuquf.
2
Note the circumstances
The three circumstances are sleeping (na'im), unconsciousness (mughma 'alayh), and ignorance of the location (lam ya'lam annaha Arafah). Recognize that all involve lack of awareness.
Ignorance here includes not knowing that one is inside Arafat.
3
Identify the essential condition
The common factor is physical presence within Arafat. No additional condition of consciousness or knowledge is mentioned. The condition for validity is simply being present geographically.
Time condition (prescribed time) is assumed; this text does not address timing.
4
Identify what is not required
The explicit inclusion of these states shows that intention (niyyah) for wuquf and awareness are not conditions. The ruling is a clear exception to the general principle that acts of worship require consciousness.
Contrast with other rituals like prayer where consciousness is required.
5
Compare with other schools
The Shafi'i school requires consciousness for wuquf. Note that the Hanafi view is based on the hadith 'the whole of Arafat is a standing place' and the act's nature as a physical presence.
This ikhtilaf affects pilgrims who become unconscious during Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ اجْتَازَ بِعَرَفَةَ وَهُوَ نَائِمٌ أَوْ مُغْمًى عَلَيْهِ أَوْ لَمْ يَعْلَمْ أَنَّهَا عَرَفَةُ أَجْزَاهُ ذَلِكَ عَنْ الْوُقُوفِ.
And whoever passes by Arafat while he is asleep or unconscious or does not know that it is Arafat, that suffices for him for the standing.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This ruling confirms that the validity of wuquf (standing at Arafat) depends solely on physical presence within the boundaries of Arafat during the prescribed time. Consciousness, awareness, or intention to stand are not required. Therefore, if a person is asleep, unconscious, or unaware of the location, their presence still counts as wuquf and their Hajj is valid. The Hanafi school relies on the principle that the pillar (rukn) of Hajj is being present at Arafat, not a specific mental state.

Key Terms
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness, a state where a person loses awareness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person falls asleep inside the boundaries of Arafat during the time of wuquf and does not wake up until after the time ends. Is his Hajj valid?
A) No, because he was not awake.
B) Yes, because physical presence suffices.
C) No, because he did not intend.
D) It depends on his intention before sleeping.

Key Takeaway
Physical presence in Arafat alone suffices for wuquf; consciousness, awareness, and intention are not required.

Women's Rites in Hajj: The Five Exceptions
List of five differences for women in Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five differences for women in Hajj and explain the Hanafi reasoning for each.

Core Idea
In Hajj, women follow men's rites except for five modesty-based exceptions: cover head, quiet talbiyah, no ramal, no running in sa'i, and face uncovered.

This lesson outlines the specific rulings for women during Hajj as per the Hanafi school. While women generally perform the same rituals as men, there are five key exceptions grounded in the principle of modesty (sitr) and avoiding fitna. Understanding these differences ensures women can perform Hajj correctly while maintaining their prescribed decorum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recognize that the default rule is equality: women perform all rites like men.
2
List the Five Exceptions
Memorize the five actions women do differently: cover head, uncover face, quiet talbiyah, no ramal, no running between the green pillars.
3
Understand the Underlying Principle
Each exception is based on modesty (sitr) and preventing fitna (temptation).
Modesty is the unifying reason.
4
Apply to a Scenario
Given a description of a woman performing Hajj, identify which exceptions apply and whether she is following the correct ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمَرْأَةُ فِي جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ كَالرَّجُلِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهَا لَا تَكْشِفُ رَأْسَهَا وَتَكْشِفُ وَجْهَهَا وَلَا تَرْفَعُ صَوْتَهَا بِالتَّلْبِيَةِ وَلَا تَرْمُلُ فِي الطَّوَافِ وَلَا تَسْعَى بَيْنَ الْمِيلَيْنِ الْأَخْضَرَيْنِ.
And the woman in all of that is like the man, except that she does not uncover her head and she uncovers her face, and she does not raise her voice in talbiyah, and she does not pace quickly in tawaf, and she does not run between the two green pillars.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage outlines the specific rules for women in Hajj, establishing that generally women follow the same rites as men, but with five exceptions: (1) She must cover her head (like in regular prayer) but may uncover her face (unlike in prayer where she covers it). (2) She recites the talbiyah quietly, not loudly, to avoid attracting attention. (3) She does not perform ramal (a brisk walk with shoulder movement) during tawaf. (4) She does not run between the two green markers (milayn akhdarayn) in sa'i. These exceptions are based on modesty and to prevent fitna. The Hanafi school considers these rules as sunnah, and violating them without reason is makruh tanzih.

Key Terms
الرمَل (ar-ramal): Walking with a brisk pace while moving the shoulders, done by men in the first three rounds of tawaf.
الميلان الأخضران (al-milayn al-akhdarayn): Two green markers in the Sa'i area where men run; women walk normally.
التلبية (at-talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by pilgrims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a difference for women in Hajj compared to men?
A) She must raise her voice in talbiyah.
B) She must cover her head and uncover her face.
C) She must perform ramal in tawaf.
D) She must run between the green pillars.

Key Takeaway
Women in Hajj follow men's rites with five exceptions based on modesty: covering head, uncovering face, quiet talbiyah, no ramal, no running in sa'i.

Women Only Trim Hair When Exiting Ihram
Ruling with explicit dalil from Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hair removal for women exiting ihram and cite the primary hadith proof.

Core Idea
Women exit ihram by trimming hair, not shaving — the Prophet explicitly exempted them from halq.

Exiting the state of ihram requires a final act of hair removal, but the ruling differs for men and women. While men may shave or trim, women are instructed to trim only. This lesson examines the primary textual proof from the Sunnah and the Hanafi position derived from it.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
Identify the act in question (hair removal upon exiting ihram) and the specific ruling for women: she must trim (taqsir), not shave (halq).
The ruling is derived from the hadith below.
2
Examine the primary dalil
Read the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'Women are not required to shave; only trimming is required of women.' Note the negation of halq and the affirmation of taqsir.
This is a sahih hadith recorded by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'halq' is negated, indicating prohibition or lack of obligation for women; 'taqsir' is affirmed, establishing it as the required act. In Hanafi usul, a negative command (laysa) here implies impermissibility or absence of requirement, and the positive command (innama) indicates obligation (wujub).
The dalala (indication) is zanni, but sufficient to establish the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with other madhahib
Some other schools permit or even prefer shaving for women, but the Hanafi school holds taqsir as wajib. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: a woman who shaves would be valid but sinful according to Hanafis.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is often say taqsir is sufficient but shaving is also permissible.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
A woman trims at least a fingertip length from the ends of her hair. She does not need to shave any part of her head.
The exact amount is specified in the Urdu commentary as 'a fingertip length.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا تَحْلِقُ رَأْسَهَا وَلَكِنْ تُقَصِرُ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تَحْلِقُ رَأْسَهَا وَلَكِنْ تُقَصِّرُ \ أَنَّ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَيْسَ عَلَى النِّسَاءِ حَلْقٌ إِنَّمَا عَلَى النِّسَاءِ التَّقْصِيرُ» (ابو داؤد: بَابُ مَنْ لَم يُدْرِكْ عَرَفَةَ، نمبر : 1950/ الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أَدْرَكَ الإِمَامَ بِجَمْعِ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الْحَجَّ،
نمبر: 891)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تَحْلِقُ رَأْسَهَا وَلَكِنْ تُقَصِرُ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى النِّسَاءَ فِي إِحْرَامِهِنَّ عَنِ القُفَّازَيْنِ وَالنِّقَابِ، وَمَا مَسَّ الْوَرْسُ وَالزَّعْفَرَانُ مِنَ القِيَابِ، وَلْتَلْبَسْ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مَا أَحَبَّتْ مِنْ أَلْوَانِ القِيَابِ مُعَصْفَرًا أَوْ خَرًّا أَوْ حُلِيًّا أَوْ سَرَاوِيلَ أَوْ قَمِيصًا أَوْ خُفَّا». ابو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يَلْبَسُ الْمُحْرِمُ، نمبر: 1827) اصول: خواتین ان تمام احکام میں مرد ہی کی طرح شامل ہیں البتہ عورت کا احرام چہرے میں ہے بایں طور کہ چہرہ کھلا رکھے ، کپڑا مس نہ ہونے دے، نیز آواز پست رکھے ، اور رمل اور میلین اخضرین میں تیز نہ دوڑے۔ اصول: خواتین سر کے بالوں کا حلق نہ کرائے بلکہ تقصیر کرائے گی، اور ایک پوروے کے برابر بال کاٹ لے۔
And she does not shave her head, but she trims.
Proof (1): Hadith for establishing (the ruling)... that Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Women are not required to shave; only trimming is required of women.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi)
Proof (2): Hadith... from Abdullah ibn Umar that he heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ forbid women in ihram from wearing gloves and niqab, and garments touched with wars or saffron, and that they may wear after that any colors they like: dyed, silk, jewelry, trousers, shirt, or khuff. (Abu Dawud) 
Principles: Women are included in all these rules like men, except that a woman's ihram is in her face, meaning she keeps her face uncovered and does not let cloth touch it; also she keeps her voice low, and does not run during ramal or between the two green markers. Principles: Women should not shave their head, but will perform taqsir (trimming), and cut an amount equal to a fingertip.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof regarding women exiting the state of ihram. The core ruling is that a woman does not shave her head (halq) but only trims (taqsir) her hair. The first proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet ﷺ explicitly says that shaving is not required for women; only trimming is required. The second proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar listing prohibitions for women in ihram (gloves, niqab, scented clothes) but does not directly address shaving; it is cited as supporting evidence for the general principle that women have different rules. The passage ends with a Urdu summary explaining that women are like men in most rulings of hajj, except for the specific exemptions: face uncovered, low voice, no running, and trimming instead of shaving. The amount of trimming is specified as about a fingertip length.

Key Terms
تقصير (taqsir): Trimming the hair by cutting a small portion (about a fingertip length) from the ends.
حلق (halq): Shaving the entire head, prescribed for men but not for women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She must shave her entire head.
B) She must trim her hair by at least a fingertip length.
C) She must let her hair grow without cutting.
D) She must cut her hair very short like a man's.

Key Takeaway
Women exit ihram by trimming at least a fingertip length of hair; shaving is not an option based on explicit prophetic instruction.

Why Hanafis Consider Qiran Superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad
Matn with hadith proofs and madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the superiority of Qiran, cite the three primary hadith proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram (Qiran) is superior because the Prophet explicitly commanded it.

The Hanafi school holds that Qiran—combining Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram from the miqat—is the most virtuous form of pilgrimage. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i preference for Ifrad and the Maliki preference for Tamattu'. By the end, you will see why the Hanafis prioritize the Prophet's direct command to enter ihram for 'Umrah within Hajj.'

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: Qiran is afdal (superior) to Tamattu' and Ifrad. Describe the Qiran procedure: ihram for both from the miqat, intention after prayer.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proofs
Examine the three ahadith: from Umar (command 'qul 'umratan fi hajjah'), from Anas (Prophet's talbiyah for both), and from Umm Salamah (command to the family). Each shows prophetic approval of combining.
Understand the wajh al-dalalah: the command (amr) indicates preference or obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Identify the opposing school and their proofs
Shafi'i: Prophet performed Ifrad (hadith of Aisha). Maliki: the verse {faman tamatta'a...} suggests Tamattu' is the norm.
Know the opposing proofs to understand the dispute.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The ahadith commanding combination are more numerous and specific; the Prophet's practice on multiple occasions confirms preference. The verse about Tamattu' does not negate Qiran's superiority; it regulates Tamattu' when chosen.
The Hanafi tarjih relies on specificity and multiple corroborating reports.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Hanafis recommend Qiran; Shafi'is recommend Ifrad; Malikis recommend Tamattu'. The rituals differ in sequence and sacrifice requirements. The fatwa in Hanafi school is that Qiran is superior.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf—the practical difference in recommended practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْقِرَانِ
بَابُ الْقِرَانِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - الْقِرَانُ عِنْدَنَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ التَّمَتُّع وَالْإِفْرَادِ وَصِفَةُ الْقِرَانِ أَنْ يُهِنَّ بِالْعُمْرَةِ وَالْحَجِّ مَعًا مِنْ الْمِيقَاتِ وَيَقُولُ عَقِيبَ الصَّلَاةِ اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أُرِيدُ الْعُمْرَةَ وَالْحَجَّ فَيَسِرْهُمَا لِي وَتَقَبَّلْهُمَا مِنِّي
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت الْقِرَانُ عِنْدَنَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ التَّمَتُّع وَالْإِفْرَادِ سَمِعَ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، يَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِوَادِي العَقِيقِ يَقُولُ: "أَتَانِي اللَّيْلَةَ آتِ مِنْ رَبِّي، فَقَالَ: صَلِّ فِي هَذَا الوَادِي الْمُبَارَكِ، وَقُلْ عُمْرَةً فِي حَجَّةٍ" (بخاري: بَابُ قَوْلِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «العَقِيقُ وَادٍ مُبَارَكٌ»، نمبر 1534/ أبو داؤد بَابٌ في الإِقْرَانِ نمبر: 1800)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت الْقِرَانُ عِنْدَنَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ التَّمَتُّع وَالْإِفْرَادِ عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ، أَنَّهُم سَمِعُوهُ يَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يُلَبِّي بِالْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ جَمِيعًا، يَقُولُ: «لَبَّيْكَ عُمْرَةً وَحَجَّا، لَبَّيْكَ عُمْرَةً وَحَجَّا» (ابو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي الْإِقْرَانِ، نمبر : 1795/ 1232)
وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت الْقِرَانُ عِنْدَنَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ التَّمَتُّعِ وَالْإِفْرَادِ فَدَخَلْتُ عَلَى أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا ... سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: "أَهِلُوا يَا آلَ مُحَمَّدٍ بِعُمْرَةٍ فِي حَجَّةٍ" (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ الْعُمْرَةِ قَبْلَ الْحَجِّ وَالْحَجِّ قَبْلَ الْعُمْرَةِ، نمبر : 8786)
وجه:(1) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت الْقِرَانُ عِنْدَنَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ التَّمَتُّعِ وَالْإِفْرَادِ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَامَ حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ، مَنْ أَهَلَّ بِعُمْرَةٍ، وَمِنَّا مَنْ أَهَلَّ بِحَجَّةٍ وَعُمْرَةٍ، وَمِنَّا مَنْ أَهَلَّ بِالْحَجِّ «وَأَهَلَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِالْحَجِّ» ، فَأَمَّا مَنْ أَهَلَّ بِالْحَجِّ أَوْ جَمَعَ الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لَمْ يَحِلُّوا حَتَّى كَانَ يَوْمُ النَّحْرِ (بخاري: بَابُ التَّمَتُّع وَالإِقْرَانِ وَالإِفْرَادِ بِالْحَجِّ : 1562/ أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي إِفْرَادِ الْحَجِّ: 1777، 1779)
وجه (۲) دليل الشافعي الآية لثبوت الْقِرَانُ عِنْدَنَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ التَّمَتُّعِ وَالْإِفْرَادِ {فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ} (سورة البقرة، 2 الاية نمبر: 196)
اصول : ایک ہی سفر میں حج کے ساتھ عمرہ کا بھی احرام باندھے تو یہ قرآن کہلاتا ہے. اصول : احناف قرآن کو افضل کہتے ہیں تمتع اور افراد سے جبکہ امام شافعی افراد کو اور امام مالک تمتع کو .
Chapter of Qiran. He said - may Allah have mercy on him - Qiran according to us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad. The description of Qiran is that he enters ihram for Umrah and Hajj together from the miqat and says after the prayer: O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me. Evidence (1): Hadith for establishing that Qiran according to us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad: He heard Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) say: I heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Wadi al-Aqiq say: 'Last night a messenger from my Lord came to me and said: Pray in this blessed valley and say: Umrah within Hajj.' (Bukhari and Abu Dawud). Evidence (2): Hadith for establishing that Qiran according to us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad: From Anas ibn Malik that they heard him say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) reciting talbiyah for both Hajj and Umrah together, saying: 'Labbaik Umrah and Hajj, Labbaik Umrah and Hajj.' (Abu Dawud). Evidence (3): Hadith for establishing that Qiran according to us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad: I entered upon Umm Salamah (may Allah be pleased with her)... I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Enter ihram, O family of Muhammad, for Umrah within Hajj.' (Bayhaqi). Evidence (1) of Shafi'i's proof: Hadith for establishing Qiran according to us is better than Tamattu' and Ifrad? Actually this is Shafi'i's evidence: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that she said: We went out with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage; some of us entered ihram for Umrah, some for Hajj and Umrah, and some for Hajj, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) entered ihram for Hajj. As for those who entered ihram for Hajj or combined Hajj and Umrah, they did not come out of ihram until the day of Nahr. (Bukhari, Abu Dawud). Evidence (2) of Shafi'i's proof: The verse: {So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj, then [offer] whatever is easy of sacrificial animal} (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:196). Principle: If he ties ihram for both Hajj and Umrah in one journey, this is called Qiran. Principle: Hanafis say Qiran is superior to Tamattu' and Ifrad, while Imam Shafi'i says Ifrad is superior and Imam Malik says Tamattu' is superior.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn establishes the Hanafi ruling that Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) is superior (afdal) to both Tamattu' (performing Umrah first, then Hajj with a separate ihram) and Ifrad (performing only Hajj). The author then provides the description of Qiran: entering ihram for both from the miqat and making the intention after prayer. The commentary adds three hadith proofs for the Hanafi position: from Umar (command to say 'Umrah within Hajj'), from Anas (the Prophet's talbiyah for both), and from Umm Salamah (command to the family of Muhammad to enter ihram for Umrah within Hajj). These show the Prophet's practice and command. Then two proofs from the Shafi'i school are cited: the hadith of Aisha indicating the Prophet performed Ifrad, and the verse about Tamattu' suggesting that Tamattu' is the primary form. The usul notes clarify the definition of Qiran and summarize the madhhab dispute: Hanafis prefer Qiran, Shafi'is prefer Ifrad, Malikis prefer Tamattu'. This illustrates how the Hanafi school relies on specific prophetic commands that combine the two rites.

Key Terms
الْقِرَان (al-qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram from the miqat.
التَّمَتُّع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah first in the months of Hajj, then Hajj separately in the same year, with a sacrifice.
الْإِفْرَاد (al-ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without Umrah in the same journey.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which form of Hajj is considered the most virtuous?
A) Ifrad
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Qiran as the superior form of Hajj because the Prophet explicitly commanded and practiced combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram.

Actions of the Qarin: Two Tawafs vs One - The Hanafi Position
Inter-madhhab dispute on number of tawafs and sa'is for the qarin, and the wajib sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi sequence of rituals for a qarin, state the evidence for two tawafs, and defend the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
A qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'is; one for Umrah, one for Hajj, and must sacrifice an animal.

The qarin (one performing Qiran) has a specific set of rituals upon entering Makkah. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi sequence: first the actions of Umrah, then the actions of Hajj. We will also examine the inter-madhhab dispute on whether a single tawaf suffices, and the evidence for the required sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Umrah actions
The qarin begins with tawaf (with ramal in first three circuits) and sa'i between Safa and Marwah for Umrah.
These are the same actions as a mutamatti.
2
Identify the Hajj actions
After Umrah, the qarin performs tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) and another sa'i between Safa and Marwah for Hajj.
This is in addition to the tawaf al-ifadah later.
3
Locate the sacrifice requirement
On the Day of Nahr, after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah, he slaughters an animal (sheep, cow, camel, or share). This is dam al-qiran.
The sacrifice is wajib.
4
Analyze the dispute on tawafs
The Shafi'i school holds only one tawaf suffices, citing Aisha's hadith. The Hanafi school holds two, citing Ali's hadith and the matn.
Both hadith are authentic; the dispute is over interpretation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Hanafis respond that Aisha's hadith likely refers to the Umrah tawaf, and the Prophet's practice supports two tawafs for the qarin.
The Hanafi position is presented as mufta bihi in this text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ ابْتَدَأَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ يَرْمُلُ فِي الثَّلَاثِ الْأُوَلِ وَيَسْعَى بَعْدَهَا بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ وَهَذِهِ أَفْعَالُ الْعُمْرَةِ ٣ ثُمَّ يَطُوفُ بَعْدَهَا طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ وَيَسْعَى بين الصفا والمروة للحج كمابيناه في حق المفرد فَإِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةً أَوْ بَدَنَةً أَوْ بَقَرَةً أَوْ سُبعَ بَدَنَةٍ أَوْ سُبُعَ بَقَرَةٍ وَهَذَا دَمُ الْقِرَانِ
لوجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ ابْتَدَأَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: قَدِمَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ لِأَرْبَعِ لَيَالٍ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: اجْعَلُوهَا عُمْرَةً إِلَّا مَنْ كَانَ مَعَهُ الْهَدْيَ (ابو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي إِفْرَادِ الْحَجِّ، نمبر: 1788)
وجه:(۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ ابْتَدَأَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: «كَانَتْ لَنَا رُخْصَةً» يَعْنِي الْمُتْعَةَ فِي الْحَجِّ (مسلم: بَابُ جَوَازِ التَّمَتُّعِ، نمبر: 1224)
وجه:(۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت ثُمَّ يَطُوفُ بَعْدَهَا طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ عَنْ عَلِيِّ أَنَّهُ جَمَعَ بَيْنَ الْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ، فَطَافَ فَمَا طَوَافَا وَاحِدًا وَسَعَى هُمَا سَعْيَيْنِ (سنن الدار قطني : كِتَاب الْحَجِّ، نمبر : 2628)
وجه:(1) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَطُوفُ بَعْدَهَا طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ ... وَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ جَمَعُوا بَيْنَ الْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ، فَإِنَّمَا طَافُوا طَوَافًا وَاحِدًا (بخاري: بَابُ طَوَافِ القَارِنِ نمبر: 1638/ مسلم: بَابُ بَيَانِ التَّحَلُّلِ بِالْإِحْصَارِ وَجَوَازِ الْقِرَانِ نمبر: 1230)
توجه: (1) الأية لثبوت فَإِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةً {فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ} (سورة البقرة، 2 الاية نمبر: 196)
وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةً عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، أَنَّهُ سُئِلَ عَنْ مُتْعَةِ الْحَجِّ، فَقَالَ: ..... ثُمَّ أَمَرَنَا عَشِيَّةَ التَّرْوِيَةِ أَنْ نُهِلَّ بِالْحَجِّ، فَإِذَا فَرَغْنَا مِنَ الْمَنَاسِكِ، جِئْنَا فَطُفْنَا بِالْبَيْتِ، وَبِالصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ، فَقَدْ ثَمَّ حَجُّنَا وَعَلَيْنَا الْهَدْيُّ، كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ} (بخاري: بَابُ قَوْلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى: {ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ أَهْلُهُ حَاضِرِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ}، نمبر : 1572)
اصول : عمرہ میں تین کام ہوتے ہیں احرام ۲ طواف ۳ سعی بین الصفاء والمروہ، لہذا قران میں اولا یہ کرے.
Then when he enters Makkah, he begins and performs tawaf around the House seven circuits, walking quickly (ramal) in the first three, and then performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah. These are the actions of Umrah. Then after that, he performs the tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum) and performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah for Hajj, as we explained for the mufrid. Then when he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep, a camel, a cow, or a seventh of a camel or a seventh of a cow. This is the blood of Qiran. Evidence (1): Hadith for establishing that when he enters Makkah, he begins and performs tawaf around the House: From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and his Companions arrived on the fourth night, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Make it Umrah, except for those who have a sacrificial animal with them.' (Abu Dawud). Evidence (2): Saying of a Companion for establishing that when he enters Makkah, he begins and performs tawaf around the House: From Abu Dharr (may Allah be pleased with him), he said: 'We had a concession' meaning Tamattu' in Hajj. (Muslim). Evidence (1): Saying of a Companion for establishing that then after that he performs tawaf al-qudum: From Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he combined Hajj and Umrah, so he performed one tawaf for both and two sa'is. (Sunan al-Daraqutni). Evidence (1): Proof of al-Shafi'i from hadith for establishing that then after that he performs tawaf al-qudum: From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): We went out with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) on the Farewell Pilgrimage... As for those who combined Hajj and Umrah, they only performed one tawaf. (Bukhari, Muslim). Evidence (1): The verse for establishing that then when he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep: {So whoever performs Tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj, then [offer] whatever is easy of sacrificial animal} (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:196). Evidence (2): Saying of a Companion for establishing that then when he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep: From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he was asked about Tamattu' of Hajj and said: ... Then he commanded us on the evening of Tarwiyah to enter ihram for Hajj, and when we finished the rituals, we came and performed tawaf around the House and between Safa and Marwah, so our Hajj was complete and we owed the sacrificial animal, as Allah said: {whatever is easy of sacrificial animal}. (Bukhari). Principle: Umrah consists of three actions: ihram, tawaf, and sa'i between Safa and Marwah. Therefore, in Qiran, one does these first.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage describes the specific sequence of rituals for a qarin (one performing Qiran) upon entering Makkah. According to the Hanafi school, the qarin first performs the actions of Umrah: tawaf (with ramal in the first three circuits) and sa'i between Safa and Marwah. Then he performs a separate tawaf al-qudum (tawaf of arrival) for Hajj, followed by another sa'i for Hajj. The text then mentions the sacrifice: after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters an animal; this is called dam al-qiran (the blood of Qiran). The commentary provides several proofs: the hadith of Jabir indicates that those without a sacrificial animal could change their intention to Umrah, implying that qarin with a sacrifice maintains his combined intention. The hadith of Abu Dharr mentions the concession of Tamattu'. For the two tawafs, the text presents a dispute: the hadith of Ali reports that he performed one tawaf and two sa'is, while the hadith of Aisha reports that those who combined did only one tawaf. The Hanafi school follows the view of two tawafs, as is evident from the matn's description. The verse of sacrifice is cited as the basis for the required blood. The usul note reminds that Umrah has three fundamental acts: ihram, tawaf, and sa'i; thus the qarin begins with these.

Key Terms
طَوَاف الْقُدُوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon first entering Makkah for Hajj, also called tawaf al-tahiyyah.
دَم الْقِرَان (dam al-qiran): The sacrificial animal required from a qarin, due to combining Hajj and Umrah.
الرَّمَل (al-ramal): Walking briskly with short steps in the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many tawafs does a qarin perform according to the Hanafi school?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The qarin must perform two tawafs (Umrah and Hajj) and two sa'is, and then sacrifice an animal as wajib.

Actions of the Qarin upon Entering Mecca
Ruling on sequence of tawaf, sa'i, and sacrifice for the qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of rituals for a qarin upon entering Mecca and identify the proofs used by the Hanafi school for two tawafs and two sa'is.

Core Idea
The qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'is: first for Umrah, then for Hajj, and must sacrifice an animal.

This passage from the chapter on Qiran outlines the required actions when a pilgrim who has combined Hajj and Umrah enters Mecca. The Hanafi school holds that the qarin must perform two separate sets of tawaf and sa'i: first for Umrah, then for Hajj. Additionally, a sacrificial animal (dam al-qiran) is wajib. The passage also responds to the Shafi'i perspective that only one tawaf is needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qarin's first action upon entering Mecca
According to the text, the qarin begins with tawaf and sa'i for Umrah—this establishes the sequence.
2
Examine the proof for performing Umrah first
The hadith of Jabir (Abu Dawud) shows the Prophet instructed those with hady to make it Umrah, which forms the basis for the Hanafi order.
The imperative 'aj'aluha' indicates command.
3
Distinguish between the two tawafs and two sa'is
After Umrah, the qarin performs tawaf al-qudum and sa'i for Hajj. Understand that this is not a single combined action but two distinct sets.
The text says 'then after that' (thumma ba'daha).
4
Analyze the proof for the second set (Hajj)
The text cites Ali's practice of performing one tawaf and two sa'is, supporting the two sa'is. Contrast with the Shafi'i reliance on Aisha's hadith.
Ali's practice is a companion action (qawl al-sahabi).
5
Determine the ruling on the sacrifice
The dam al-qiran is wajib, based on Quran 2:196 and the practice of Ibn Abbas. Identify the timing: after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr.
Sacrifice can be a sheep, camel, cow, or share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْقِرَانِ
ل فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ ابْتَدَأَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ يَرْمُلُ فِي الثَّلَاثِ الْأُوَلِ وَيَسْعَى بَعْدَهَا بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ وَهَذِهِ أَفْعَالُ الْعُمْرَةِ ٣ ثُمَّ يَطُوفُ بَعْدَهَا طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ وَيَسْعَى بي ن الصفا والمروة للحج كمابيناه في حق المفرد فَإِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةً أَوْ بَدَنَةً أَوْ بَقَرَةً أَوْ سُبعَ بَدَنَةٍ أَوْ سُبُعَ بَقَرَةٍ وَهَذَا دَمُ الْقِرَانِ لوجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ ابْتَدَأَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: قَدِمَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَصْحَابُهُ لِأَرْبَعِ لَيَالٍ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: اجْعَلُوهَا عُمْرَةً إِلَّا مَنْ كَانَ مَعَهُ الْهَدْيَ ابو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي إِفْرَادِ الحَجَ، نمبر: 1788) وجه:(۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ ابْتَدَأَ فَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ \ عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: «كَانَتْ لَنَا رُخْصَةً» يَعْنِي الْمُتْعَةَ فِي الْحَجَّ (مسلم: بَابُ جَوَازِ التَّمَتُّعِ، نمبر: 1224 وجه:(۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت ثُمَّ يَطُوفُ بَعْدَهَا طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ عَنْ عَلِيِّ أَنَّهُ جَمَعَ بَيْنَ الْحَجِ وَالْعُمْرَةِ ، فَطَافَ فَمَا طَوَافَا وَاحِدًا وَسَعَى هُمَا سَعْيَيْنِ (سنن الدار قطني : كِتَاب الحج، نمبر : 2628 وجه:(1) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَطُوفُ بَعْدَهَا طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ أَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ ... وَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ جَمَعُوا بَيْنَ الْحَجَّ وَالعُمْرَةِ، فَإِنَّمَا طَافُوا طَوَافًا وَاحِدًا (بخاري بَابُ طَوَافِ القَارِنِ نمبر: 1638/ مسلم: بَابُ بَيَانِ التَّحَلُّل بِالْإِحْصَارِ وَجَوَازِ الْقِرَانِ نمبر: 1230 توجه: (1) الأية لثبوت فَإِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةَ \ ﴿فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي (سورة البقرة، 2ألاية نمبر: 196) وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةً \ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا ، أَنَّهُ سُئِلَ عَنْ مُتْعَةِ الحَجَ، فَقَالَ : ..... ثُمَّ أَمَرَنَا عَشِيَّةَ التَّرْوِيَةِ أَنْ تُمِل بِالحَجَ، فَإِذَا فَرَغْنَا مِنَ المَنَاسِكِ، جِئْنَا فَطْفْنَا بِالْبَيْتِ ، وَبِالصَّفَا وَالمَرْوَةِ، فَقَدْ ثَمَّ حَجُنَا وَعَلَيْنَا الهَدْيُّ، كَمَا قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: {فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الهَدْيِ، (بخاري بَابُ قَوْلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى: {ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ أَهْلُهُ. حَاضِرِي المَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ}، نمبر : 1572) اصول : عمرہ میں تین کام ہوتے ہیں ااحرام ۲ طواف ۳ سعی بین الصفاء والمروہ، لہذا قران میں اولا یہ کرے.
Chapter of Qiran. When he enters Mecca, he begins and performs tawaf around the House seven circuits, walking briskly (ramal) in the first three, and then performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah. These are the actions of Umrah. Then after that he performs tawaf al-qudum and performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah for Hajj, as we explained in the case of ifrad. Then when he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep, a camel, a cow, or a seventh of a camel or a seventh of a cow. This is the blood of qiran. For evidence: (1) The hadith to prove 'when he enters Mecca, he begins and performs tawaf around the House' from Jabir: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) arrived with his Companions with four nights remaining... (Abu Dawud) (2) The saying of a companion to prove 'when he enters Mecca, he begins and performs tawaf around the House' from Abu Dharr: 'We had a concession' meaning tamattu' in Hajj (Muslim) (1) The saying of a companion to prove 'then he performs tawaf al-qudum after it' from Ali: he combined Hajj and Umrah, performed one tawaf and two sa'is (al-Daraqutni) (1) The proof of al-Shafi'i is the hadith to prove 'then he performs tawaf al-qudum after it' from Aisha: we went out with the Prophet... but those who combined Hajj and Umrah performed only one tawaf (Bukhari, Muslim) (1) The verse to prove 'when he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep': {Whoever performs tamattu' by Umrah to Hajj, then the easiest of sacrifice} (al-Baqarah 2:196) (2) The saying of a companion to prove 'when he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep' from Ibn Abbas: he was asked about tamattu' and said: ... then he commanded us on the evening of Tarwiyah to enter into Hajj... so we had performed Hajj and had to offer sacrifice (Bukhari) Principle: Umrah consists of three actions: 1. Ihram, 2. Tawaf, 3. Sa'i between Safa and Marwah. Therefore, the qarin should do these first.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the chapter on Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah). The matn states that a qarin, upon entering Mecca, first performs Umrah: tawaf with ramal in the first three circuits, then sa'i between Safa and Marwah. After completing Umrah, he performs tawaf al-qudum (the arrival tawaf) and sa'i for Hajj, as explained earlier for the ifrad pilgrim. On the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), after throwing the Jamrat al-Aqabah, he slaughters a sacrificial animal—a sheep, camel, cow, or one-seventh of a camel or cow. This is called the dam al-qiran (the blood of qiran), which is wajib upon the qarin. The text then provides multiple proofs: (1) The hadith of Jabir where the Prophet instructed his companions to make their ihram for Umrah unless they had brought a sacrificial animal, establishing that the qarin (who has the hady) should perform Umrah first. (2) The saying of Abu Dharr that tamattu' was a concession. (3) Ali's practice of performing one tawaf and two sa'is supports the Hanafi view that the qarin does two sa'is. (4) The Shafi'i argument from Aisha that the Prophet and others performed only one tawaf is acknowledged but countered by the Hanafi interpretation that this refers to tawaf al-qudum, not the Umrah tawaf. (5) Quranic verse 2:196 is cited for the sacrifice. (6) Ibn Abbas's hadith about the command on Tarwiyah day. The Urdu summary at the end reiterates that Umrah has three components: ihram, tawaf, and sa'i, and the qarin should begin with these.

Key Terms
القِران (al-qiran): A form of ihram where one combines the intentions for both Hajj and Umrah simultaneously, entering ihram for both with a single talbiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does the qarin perform first upon entering Mecca?
A) Tawaf al-qudum for Hajj
B) Tawaf and sa'i for Umrah
C) Ramy al-Jamarat
D) Sa'i only

Key Takeaway
The qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa'is (Umrah first, then Hajj) and sacrifice an animal, with proofs from hadith, companion practice, and the Quran.

Fasting Substitute for the Qarin's Sacrifice
Ruling with proofs on the fasting substitute for the qarin's sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fasting substitute for the qarin's sacrifice and identify the key conditions, timing, and proofs from the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
When a qarin cannot afford a sacrifice, fasting three days during Hajj (ending on Arafah) and seven after returning becomes wajib.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents the ruling for a qarin who cannot slaughter a sacrificial animal. The text not only states the substitute but also anchors it in Quranic and prophetic proofs, showing how the Hanafi school derives this obligation. Understanding this ruling is essential for anyone performing Hajj as a qarin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its trigger
The ruling applies when the qarin cannot afford a sacrifice. The substitute is fasting. Determine the hukm level: wajib, not fard, because it is a replacement for a wajib dam.
Note: The inability to afford must be genuine; if one can afford, the sacrifice is still wajib.
2
Determine the timing of the three fasts
They must be during the days of Hajj, with the last day being the day of Arafah. This is because fasting on the days of Tashreeq (11th-13th) is prohibited, as cited in the hadiths.
The three days can be the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul Hijjah, or the 8th, 9th, and 10th? But the 10th is Eid, so prohibited. So effectively the three are before the day of Nahr.
3
Understand the consequence if the three fasts are missed
If the three days expire without fasting (e.g., because the qarin was unable to fast or arrived late), then he must fast seven days after returning home. These can be any seven consecutive or separate days.
The missed three-day fast does not become qada; it is replaced by the seven-day fast.
4
Examine the proofs
The primary proof is Quran 2:196 for tamattu', and qarin is analogized to tamattu'. Additional supporting arguments include hadiths prohibiting fasting on Eid and Tashreeq, and companion sayings specifying the timing and necessity.
The hadith of Jabir about sharing a sacrifice is used to define the form of hady, not directly the fasting substitute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجَ آخِرُهَا يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ فَإِنْ فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ ثُمَّ يَصُومُ سَبْعَةَ أَيَّامٍ إِذَا رَجَعَ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ كِ
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةً \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: «تَخَرْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَامَ الْحَدَيْبِيَةِ الْبَدَنَةَ عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، وَالْبَقَرَةَ عَنْ سَبْعَةِ» (مسلم: بَابُ الِاشْتِرَاكِ فِي الْهَدْيِ وَإِجْزَاءِ الْبَقَرَةِ وَالْبَدَنَةِ كُلَّ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، نمبر: 1318/ أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي الْبَقَرِ وَالْجُرُورِ عَنْ كَمْ تُجْزِئُ؟، نمبر : 2809)
د وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ ا ﴿فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَج فَمَا أَسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي (سورة البقرة، 2 ألاية نمبر: 196)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ \ عَنْ عُقْبَةَ بْنَ عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ، وَيَوْمُ النَّحْرِ، وَأَيَّامُ التَّشْرِيقِ عِيدُنَا أَهْلَ الْإِسْلَامِ، وَهِيَ أَيَّامُ أَكْلِ وَشُرْبِ» أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِيَامٍ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ، نمبر: 2419/ مسلم: بَابُ تَحْرِيم صَوْمِ أَيَّام التشريق، نمبر: 1141
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ \ قَالَ: «إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى عَنْ صِيَامٍ هَذَيْنِ الْيَوْمَيْنِ، أَمَّا يَوْمُ الْأَضْحَى فَتَأْكُلُونَ مِنْ لَحْمٍ نُسُكِكُمْ، وَأَمَّا يَوْمُ الْفِطْرِ فَفِطْرُكُمْ مِنْ صِيَامِكُمْ» (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي صَوْمِ الْعِيدَيْن، نمبر: 2416/
توجه:(۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ ثُمَّ يَصُومُ سَبْعَةَ أَيَّامٍ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا لَمْ يَصْمِ الْمُتَمَتِّعُ، فَعَلَيْهِ الْهَدْيُ». . . عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «لَا بُدَّ مِنْ دَمٍ وَلَوْ يَبِيعُ ثَوْبَهُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة : فِي الْمُتَمَتِّعِ إِذَا فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ، نمبر: 12985، 12989)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ ثُمَّ يَصُومُ سَبْعَةَ أَيَّامٍ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «الصَّيَامُ لِمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الحَجَ إِلَى يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ هَدْيَا وَلَمْ يَصُمْ، صَامَ أَيَّامَ مِنْى» (بخاري بَابُ صِيَامٍ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ، نمبر: 1999/) اصول : قارن اور متمتع پر ہدی لازم ہے ، اور ہدی کی صورت یہ ہے ایک بکری ہو یا ایک گائے ہو یا ایک اونٹ ہو، یا اونٹ و گائے کا ساتواں حصہ.
If he does not have anything to slaughter, he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of which is the day of Arafah. If the fast is missed (elapses), then he fasts seven days when he returns to his family. Evidence: (3) Hadith to prove 'when he throws the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep' from Jabir: we sacrificed a camel for seven and a cow for seven (Muslim, Abu Dawud). And evidence: (1) The verse to prove 'if he does not have anything to slaughter, he fasts three days': {Whoever performs tamattu'... then the easiest of sacrifice} (al-Baqarah 2:196). (2) The hadith to prove... from Uqbah: the Messenger said: 'The day of Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashreeq are our festivals... they are days of eating and drinking' (Abu Dawud, Muslim). (3) The hadith: 'He forbade fasting these two days: the day of Adha and the day of Fitr' (Abu Dawud). (1) The saying of the companion to prove 'if he missed the fast, then he fasts seven days' from Ibn Abbas: 'If the mutamatti' does not fast, then he must offer sacrifice'... from Ibrahim: 'There must be blood even if he sells his garment' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). (2) The saying of the companion to prove 'if he missed the fast, then he fasts seven days' from Ibn Umar: 'The fasting for mutamatti' is until the day of Arafah; if he cannot find a sacrifice and does not fast, he fasts the days of Mina' (Bukhari). Principle: The qarin and mutamatti' must offer sacrifice, and the form of sacrifice is: one sheep, one cow, one camel, or a seventh of a camel or cow.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the fasting substitute for the qarin's sacrifice. The matn states that if the qarin cannot afford a sacrificial animal, he must fast three days during the days of Hajj, with the last of these three being the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah). If he misses this fast (i.e., the three days pass without fasting), then he fasts seven days after returning to his family. The text provides several proofs: (1) The hadith of Jabir about sharing a camel or cow among seven people, which establishes the validity of sacrificing a seventh of a large animal. (2) The Quranic verse 2:196, which is the primary evidence for the obligation of sacrifice for tamattu' and by analogy for qiran. (3) Hadith prohibiting fasting on the days of Eid and Tashreeq, indicating that the three fasts must be before the day of Nahr, as the last day is Arafah (which is allowed), but the days of Tashreeq (11th-13th) cannot be fasted. (4) Sayings of companions: Ibn Abbas and Ibrahim emphasize that the sacrifice is obligatory and cannot be replaced except with fasting. Ibn Umar specifies that the fasting for mutamatti' is until Arafah, and if not possible, he fasts the days of Mina (which is a dispensation). The Urdu summary at the end clarifies that both the qarin and mutamatti' must offer sacrifice, and the animal can be a sheep, cow, camel, or one-seventh of a large animal.

Key Terms
الهَدْي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal (sheep, camel, cow, or one-seventh of the latter) offered in the Haram during Hajj as a wajib obligation for the qarin and mutamatti'.
الصوم (al-sawm): Fasting as a substitute for hady: three days during Hajj (the last being the day of Arafah) and seven days after returning home. This is wajib when one cannot afford a sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a qarin who cannot afford a sacrifice?
A) He must sacrifice anyway, even if he has to borrow money.
B) He must fast three days during Hajj (last day Arafah) and seven days after returning.
C) He must feed sixty poor people instead.
D) No substitute is allowed; he must skip the qiran and do ifrad.

Key Takeaway
The fasting substitute for a qarin's sacrifice is three days during Hajj (culminating on Arafah) and seven after return, and it becomes wajib when one cannot afford the hady.

Substitution of Hady with Fasting: Timing and Proofs
Ruling on substituting hady with fasting, with Quranic and Hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting as a substitute for hady, identify the required timing, and explain the Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
If you cannot afford a sacrifice, fasting substitutes — three days during Hajj ending at Arafah, and seven more after returning.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on what a pilgrim performing tamattu' or qiran must do if he cannot afford the obligatory sacrifice (hady). The Qur'an explicitly commands fasting as an alternative, and the school provides detailed timing based on hadith and companion practice. We will walk through the primary proof from Surah al-Baqarah and the secondary proofs that define the permissible fasting days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the ruling concerns fasting as a substitute for hady when one lacks the means to sacrifice. The act is wajib fasting.
The text says 'if he does not have what to slaughter, he fasts' — this establishes the substitution.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verse (2:196) that mandates fasting for those unable to sacrifice. Understand that the imperative form indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
The verse says 'fasayamu' — the command to fast.
3
Understand the timing conditions
The fast is divided: three days during Hajj, the last of which must be the day of Arafah; and seven days after returning home if the three-day fast was missed.
The day of Arafah is the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah.
4
Evaluate the secondary proofs
The text cites hadith prohibiting fasting on Eid al-Adha and the days of Tashriq, which restrict the timing. Also, companion sayings support fasting on the days of Mina for those without hady.
These proofs clarify that fasting is not allowed on prohibited days.
5
Note the additional Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi school permits fasting the three days in Makkah after completing Hajj, relying on Ibn Umar's statement that permission for fasting on Tashriq is only for those without a hady.
This shows the use of companion opinion (qawl al-sahabi) as a proof.

بَابُ الْقِرَانِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجَ آخِرُهَا يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ فَإِنْ فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ ثُمَّ يَصُومُ سَبْعَةَ أَيَّامٍ إِذَا رَجَعَ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا رَمَى جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةً عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، قَالَ: «تَخَرْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَامَ الْحَدَيْبِيَةِ الْبَدَنَةَ عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، وَالْبَقَرَةَ عَنْ سَبْعَةِ» (مسلم: بَابُ الِاشْتِرَاكِ فِي الْهَدْيِ وَإِجْزَاءِ الْبَقَرَةِ وَالْبَدَنَةِ كُلَّ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، نمبر: 1318/ أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي الْبَقَرِ وَالْجُرُورِ عَنْ كَمْ تُجْزِئُ؟، غمبر : 2809)
د وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ ا ﴿فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَج فَمَا أَسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي (سورة البقرة، 2 ألاية نمبر: 196)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ عَنْ عُقْبَةَ بْنَ عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ، وَيَوْمُ النَّحْرِ، وَأَيَّامُ التَّشْرِيقِ عِيدُنَا أَهْلَ الْإِسْلَامِ، وَهِيَ أَيَّامُ أَكْلِ وَشُرْبِ» (أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِيَامٍ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ، نمبر: 2419/ مسلم: بَابُ تَحْرِيم صَوْمِ أَيَّام التشريق، نمبر: 1141)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ قَالَ: «إِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى عَنْ صِيَامٍ هَذَيْنِ الْيَوْمَيْنِ، أَمَّا يَوْمُ الْأَضْحَى فَتَأْكُلُونَ مِنْ لَحْمٍ نُسُكِكُمْ، وَأَمَّا يَوْمُ الْفِطْرِ فَفِطْرُكُمْ مِنْ صِيَامِكُمْ» (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي صَوْمِ الْعِيدَيْن، نمبر: 2416/
توجه:(۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ ثُمَّ يَصُومُ سَبْعَةَ أَيَّامٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا لَمْ يَصْمِ الْمُتَمَتِّعُ، فَعَلَيْهِ الْهَدْيُ». . . عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «لَا بُدَّ مِنْ دَمٍ وَلَوْ يَبِيعُ ثَوْبَهُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة : فِي الْمُتَمَتِّعِ إِذَا فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ، نمبر: 12985، 12989)
وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِنْ فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ ثُمَّ يَصُومُ سَبْعَةَ أَيَّامٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «الصَّيَامُ لِمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الحَجَ إِلَى يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ هَدْيَا وَلَمْ يَصُمْ، صَامَ أَيَّامَ مِنْى» (بخاري بَابُ صِيَامٍ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ، نمبر: 1999/)
اصول : قارن اور متمتع پر ہدی لازم ہے ، اور ہدی کی صورت یہ ہے ایک بکری ہو یا ایک گائے ہو یا ایک اونٹ ہو، یا اونٹ و گائے کا ساتواں حصہ.
وَإِنْ صَامَهَا بِمَكَّةَ بَعْدَ فَرَاغِهِ مِنْ الْحَجَ جَازَ عِنْدَنَا
وجه:(۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَإِنْ صَامَهَا بِمَكَّةَ بَعْدَ فَرَاغِهِ مِنْ الْحَجِّ جَازَ اعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمْ، قَالا: «لَمْ يُرَخَّصُ فِي أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ أَنْ يُصَمْنَ إِلَّا لِمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدِ الهَدْي» (بخاري: بَابُ صِيَامِ أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيقِ، نمبر: 1997/)
Chapter of Qiran. If he does not have what to slaughter, he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of which is the day of Arafah. Then if the fasting is missed, he fasts seven days when he returns to his family. Proof (3): Hadith to establish: When he throws the pebbles at Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr, he slaughters a sheep. From Jabir ibn Abdullah, he said: We sacrificed with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in the year of Hudaybiyyah a camel for seven and a cow for seven. (Muslim, Bab al-Ishtirak fi al-Hady... no. 1318; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Baqar wa al-Jurur... no. 2809) Another proof (1): The verse to establish: 'Then if he does not have what to slaughter, he fasts three days' [Quran 2:196]. Proof (2): Hadith to establish: From Uqbah ibn Amir, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The day of Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq are our festivals, O people of Islam, and they are days of eating and drinking.' (Abu Dawud, Bab Sawm Ayyam al-Tashriq, no. 2419; Muslim, Bab Tahrim Sawm Ayyam al-Tashriq, no. 1141) Proof (3): Hadith to establish: He said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade fasting on these two days: the day of Adha and the day of Fitr.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Sawm al-Eidayn, no. 2416) Attention (1): Saying of a Companion to establish: If the fasting is missed, then he fasts seven days. From Ibn Abbas, he said: 'If the mutamatti' does not fast, then he must offer a hady.' From Ibrahim, he said: 'There is no escape from a blood offering even if he sells his garment.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 12985, 12989) Proof (2): Saying of a Companion to establish: From Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them), he said: 'Fasting is for the one who performs tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj until the day of Arafah. If he does not find a hady and does not fast, he fasts the days of Mina.' (Bukhari, Bab Sawm Ayyam al-Tashriq, no. 1999) Principle: Hady is obligatory upon the qarin and mutamatti', and the form of hady is a goat, a cow, or a camel, or a seventh share of a camel or cow. And if he fasts them in Makkah after completing Hajj, it is permissible according to us. Proof (1): Saying of a Companion to establish: From Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them), he said: 'Permission to fast on the days of Tashriq was not given except to the one who did not find a hady.' (Bukhari, Bab Sawm Ayyam al-Tashriq, no. 1997).
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the Hanafi school regarding the substitution of the obligatory sacrifice (hady) with fasting for the qarin or mutamatti' who cannot afford an animal. The matn (Quduri's text) states the basic rule: if one lacks the means to sacrifice, he must fast three days during the Hajj period, the last of which is the day of Arafah, and if he misses that fasting, then he fasts seven days after returning home. The commentary then provides multiple proofs: a hadith about sharing a camel or cow among seven participants (showing that a seventh share suffices), the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:196) which mandates fasting for those unable to sacrifice, a hadith prohibiting fasting on the two Eids and the days of Tashriq (thus clarifying that fasting is not allowed on those days, so the three days must be before or after), and another hadith about the prohibition of fasting on Eid days. Additionally, the commentary cites the sayings of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar to support the ruling that if the fasting is missed, the seven days must be observed. The usul principle in Urdu explains that hady is obligatory on the qarin and mutamatti', and the acceptable animals are a goat, cow, camel, or a seventh share. The text then adds another ruling: if one fasts those days in Makkah after completing Hajj, it is permissible according to the Hanafi school, citing Ibn Umar's statement that permission to fast on days of Tashriq is only for those without a hady. This demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving rulings from primary sources and companion opinions.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj qiran, combining Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram.
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs tamattu', performing Umrah in the Hajj season and then Hajj with separate ihrams.
هدي (hady): The animal sacrificed during Hajj, obligatory for qarin and mutamatti'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the latest day on which the three-day substitute fast for hady can be completed?
A) The day of Arafah (9th Dhul-Hijjah)
B) The day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah)
C) The last day of Tashriq (13th Dhul-Hijjah)
D) The day after returning home

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that fasting substitutes for hady when sacrifice is unaffordable, with specific timing: three days during Hajj ending on Arafah, and seven days after return if missed.

The Qarin Who Abandons Umrah: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on the qarin who abandons Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a qarin proceeds to Arafat without entering Makkah, identify the proofs from hadith and usul, and apply the principle that starting a voluntary act makes its completion obligatory.

Core Idea
Proceeding to Arafat without entering Makkah constitutes rafd al-umrah, annulling the qiran sacrifice and requiring a separate dam and qada'.

When a qarin enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah, the normal sequence is to perform Umrah first. This lesson examines the scenario where he bypasses Makkah and heads directly to Arafat. According to the Hanafi school, this act constitutes 'rafd al-umrah' (abandonment of the Umrah), transforming his obligations. Instead of the qiran sacrifice, he owes a sacrifice for the abandonment and must make up the Umrah later. We will analyse the textual proofs and the usul principle that underpin this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Define the scenario
Identify the precise action: the qarin does not enter Makkah but proceeds straight to Arafat and performs wuquf.
This is the trigger for the change in obligations.
2
Identify the immediate consequences
He becomes a 'rafid' (one who rejects his Umrah). The obligation of dam al-qiran is annulled.
The qiran sacrifice is dropped because the Umrah component is effectively abandoned.
3
List the new obligations
He owes a sacrifice for the abandonment (dam li-rafd al-umrah) and must make up the Umrah (qada').
Two new wajib acts arise: a separate sacrifice and a makeup Umrah.
4
Examine the dalil
Analyse the hadith of Aisha (Bukhari, Muslim), the hadith of Jabir about the sacrifice, and the statement of Tawus.
The Prophet's command to Aisha to abandon her Umrah and later make it up, along with the sacrifice, supports the ruling.
5
Apply the usul principle
Recognise that starting a voluntary act (nafl Umrah) makes its completion obligatory according to Hanafi usul.
This principle is derived from the hadith and is key to understanding why qada' is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْخُلْ الْقَارِنُ مَكَّةَ وَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى عَرَفَاتٍ فَقَدْ صَارَ رَافِضًا لِعُمْرَتِهِ بِالْوُقُوفِ وَبَطَلَ عَنْهُ دَمُ الْقِرَانِ وَعَلَيْهِ دَمْ لِرَفْضِ الْعُمْرَةِ وَعَلَيْهِ قَضَاؤُهَا
dوجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْخُلْ الْقَارِنُ مَكَّةَ وَتَوَجَّهَ إلَى عَرَفَاتٍ أَخْبَرَتْنِي عَائِشَةُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، قَالَتْ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مُوَافِينَ لِهِلَالِ ذِي الْحَجَّةِ، وَكُنتُ مِمَّنْ أَهَلَّ بِعُمْرَةِ، فَحِضْتُ قَبْلَ أَنْ أَدْخُلَ مَكَّةَ، فَأَدْرَكَنِي يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ وَأَنَا حَائِضٌ فَشَكَوْتُ ذلِكَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، فَقَالَ: «دَعِي عُمْرَتَكِ، وَانْقُضِي رَأْسَكِ وَامْتَشِطِي، وَأَهِلِي بِالْحَجِّ» ، فَفَعَلْتُ، فَلَمَّا كَانَتْ لَيْلَةُ الحَصْبَةِ، أَرْسَلَ مَعِي عَبْدَ الرَّحْمَنِ إِلَى التَّنْعِيمِ. فَأَرْدَفَهَا، فَأَهَلَّتْ بِعُمْرَةِ مَكَانَ عُمْرَقِنَا، فَقَضَى اللَّهُ حَجَّهَا وَعُمْرَتَهَا، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ فِي شَيْءٍ مِنْ ذَلِكَ هَدْيِّ، وَلَا صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَا صَوْمٌ (بخاري: بَابُ الِاعْتِمَارِ بَعْدَ الْحَجَ بِغَيْرِ هَدْيِ، نمبر: 1786/ مسلم: بَابُ بَيَانِ وُجُوهِ الْإِحْرَامِ، وَأَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ إِفْرَادُ الْحَجَ وَالتَّمَتُّع وَالْقِرَانِ، غبر : 1211)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْخُلْ الْقَارِنُ مَكَّةَ وَتَوَجَّهَ اعَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: «ذَبَحَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ بَقَرَةً يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ (مسلم : بَابُ الاِشْتِرَاكِ فِي الْهَدْيِ ألخ: 1319)
وجه : (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْخُلُ الْقَارِنُ مَكَّةَ وَتَوَجَّهَ إِلَى عَرَفَاتٍ عَنْ طَاوُسِ، فِي الْمُحْرِمِ لِعُمْرَةِ اعْتَرَضَ لَهُ، قَالَ: «يَبْعَثُ بِهَدْيِ، ثُمَّ يَحْسِيبُ كَمْ يَسِيرُ، ثُمَّ يَحْتَاطُ بِأَيَّامٍ، ثُمَّ يَحِلُّ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة فِي الرَّجُلِ إِذَا أَهَلَّ بِعُمْرَةِ فَأُحْصِرَ، نمبر : 13080)
اصول : قارن اور متمتع کو ہدی اور روزہ کا موقع نہ ملے تو اب دو دم لازم ہونگے ایک ہدی کا دوسرا حلال ہونے کا.
اصول : اگر قارن عمرہ چھوڑ کر عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہو گیا اور وقوف عرفہ کر لیا تو عمرہ ختم ہو گیا بعد میں اس عمرہ کی قضاء لازم ہو گی اور دم بھی لازم ہو گا، اصول: غیر واجب یا غیر فرض کو شروع کر دینے سے اس کا اتمام یعنی اسکا مکمل کرنالازم اور واجب ہوتا ہے،
If the qarin does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat, then he becomes a rejecter of his Umrah by standing (at Arafat), and the sacrifice of qiran is annulled for him, and he owes a sacrifice for abandoning the Umrah, and he must make it up. Another proof (1): Hadith to establish: Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) informed me, she said: We set out with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) at the sighting of the crescent of Dhul Hijjah, and I was among those who entered ihram for Umrah. Then I menstruated before entering Makkah, and the day of Arafah came upon me while I was menstruating. I complained about that to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he said: 'Leave your Umrah, undo your hair, comb it, and make ihram for Hajj.' I did so. Then on the night of Hasbah, he sent Abd al-Rahman with me to al-Tan'im. He seated her behind him, and she made ihram for Umrah in place of her Umrah. So Allah decreed her Hajj and Umrah, and there was no hady, nor sadaqah, nor fasting in any of that. (Bukhari, Bab al-I'timar ba'd al-Hajj... no. 1786; Muslim, Bab Bayan wujuh al-Ihram... no. 1211) Proof (2): Hadith to establish: From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) slaughtered a cow on behalf of Aisha on the day of Nahr. (Muslim, Bab al-Ishtirak fi al-Hady... no. 1319) Proof (3): Saying of a follower (Tabi'i) to establish: From Tawus, regarding one in ihram for Umrah who was obstructed, he said: 'He sends a hady, then calculates how long it takes, then adds extra days, then becomes halal.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba no. 13080) Principle: When the qarin and mutamatti' do not get the opportunity for hady and fasting, then two blood offerings become obligatory: one for hady and one for becoming halal. Principle: If the qarin abandons Umrah and proceeds towards Arafat and performs standing at Arafah, then the Umrah is ended; later, making up that Umrah becomes obligatory, and a blood offering also becomes obligatory. Principle: By starting a non-obligatory or non-fard act, its completion (i.e., fulfilling it) becomes binding and obligatory.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the Hanafi school concerning a qarin who, after entering ihram for qiran, does not enter Makkah and instead proceeds directly to Arafat for the wuquf. The ruling states that by doing so, he effectively abandons the Umrah aspect of his qiran. Consequently, his obligation for the qiran sacrifice (dam al-qiran) is dropped, but he incurs two new obligations: a sacrifice for having abandoned the Umrah (dam li-rafd al-umrah) and he must make up that Umrah (qada'). The commentary provides several proofs: the hadith of Aisha where she menstruated and the Prophet told her to abandon her Umrah and make a separate Umrah later, showing that abandonment requires compensation; the hadith that the Prophet sacrificed a cow for Aisha, indicating that a sacrifice is due; and the opinion of Tawus that one who is obstructed must send a hady and calculate additional days. The usul notes in Urdu explain the principle: if the qarin fails to perform the hady and fasting on time, two blood offerings become necessary; and that starting a voluntary act makes its completion obligatory according to Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
رافض (rafid): One who abandons or rejects his Umrah by proceeding to Arafat without performing it.
دم القران (dam al-qiran): The mandatory sacrifice for the one performing Hajj qiran.
رفض العمرة (rafd al-umrah): The act of abandoning the Umrah by proceeding to Arafat without completing it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the qarin's obligations if he proceeds to Arafat without first entering Makkah?
A) He is still considered a qarin and must offer a single sacrifice.
B) He abandons his Umrah; the qiran sacrifice is annulled, and he must offer a sacrifice for abandonment and make up the Umrah.
C) He must only make up the Umrah with no additional sacrifice.
D) He becomes a mutamatti' and must change his ihram.

Key Takeaway
A qarin who goes to Arafat without entering Makkah becomes rafid al-umrah, losing the qiran sacrifice but gaining a separate dam and qada' obligation.
