Penalty for Shaving Cupping Spots in Ihram: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on penalty for shaving cupping spots with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the penalty for shaving cupping spots during ihram and explain why Abu Hanifa's view (dam) is the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Shaving the cupping site in ihram: Abu Hanifa requires a blood sacrifice; the Sahibayn say charity suffices.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the penalty for shaving the hair at the cupping site on the neck during the state of ihram. The passage presents two positions: Abu Hanifa's obligation of a blood sacrifice (dam) and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's view that only charity (sadaqah) is required. We will explore the proofs cited, understand the reasoning behind each stance, and identify which opinion is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the positions
The issue is shaving the cupping spots on the neck during ihram. According to the matn, Abu Hanifa holds that a blood sacrifice (dam) is wajib, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that charity (sadaqah) is wajib.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, meaning the disagreement is within the Hanafi school itself.
2
Identify the proofs cited
The passage provides two proofs: (1) a statement from Imam Malik in the Muwatta categorizing various hair removal acts under fidyah, and (2) a hadith from Ibn Bukaynah that the Prophet (pbuh) had cupping while in ihram.
The hadith proves the permissibility of cupping, but the ruling on shaving the hair at the cupping site is derived analogically.
3
Trace the reasoning from the proofs to the ruling
The hadith shows cupping is allowed, but shaving the hair is a separate act of removing hair, which is generally prohibited in ihram. Abu Hanifa analogizes shaving cupping spots to other prohibited hair removal that incurs dam. The Sahibayn consider the necessity of the medical act to reduce the penalty to sadaqah.
The difference in qiyas (analogy) leads to different penalty amounts.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and the reason for tarjih
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers Abu Hanifa's view, and it is the relied-upon position for fatwa. The stronger analogy is to intentional hair removal, which typically requires dam.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view: dam is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْحِنَايَاتِ فِي الْحَجّ

وَإِنْ حَلَقَ مَوَاضِعَ الْمَحَاجِمِ مِنْ الرَّقَبَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ صَدَقَةٌ

وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت ... قَالَ مَالِكٌ: " مَنْ نَتَفَ شَعَرًا مِنْ أَنْفِهِ، أَوْ مِنْ إِبْطِهِ، أَوِ اطَّلَى جَسَدَهُ بِنُورَةٍ، أَوْ يَحْلِقُ عَنْ شَجَّةٍ فِي رَأْسِهِ لِضَرُورَةِ، أَوْ يَحْلِقُ قَفَاهُ لِمَوْضِعِ الْمَحَاجِمِ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ، نَاسِيًا أَوْ جَاهِلًا إِنَّ مَنْ فَعَلَ شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْفِدْيَةُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ. وَلَا يَنْبَغِي لَهُ أَنْ يَحْلِقَ مَوْضِعَ الْمَحَاجِمِ. (المؤطأ لإمام مالك: بَابُ فِدْيَةِ مَنْ خَلَقَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَنْحَرَ، غبر (239)

وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت ... عَنِ ابْنِ بُكَيْنَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: «احْتَجَمَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ (بخاري بَابُ الحِجَامَةِ لِلْمُحْرِمِ، نمبر : 1836/ مسلم: بَابُ جَوَازِ الْحِجَامَةِ لِلْمُحْرِمِ، نمبر: 1202)
Chapter on Penalties in Hajj. And if he shaves the places of cupping from the neck, then upon him is a blood sacrifice according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: charity. Proof (1): The saying of the follower [i.e., Imam Malik] to establish: 'Whoever plucks hair from his nose, or from his armpit, or applies depilatory to his body, or shaves due to a wound on his head out of necessity, or shaves his nape for the place of cupping while in ihram, forgetfully or ignorantly — whoever does any of that, upon him is the fidyah in all of that. And it is not appropriate for him to shave the place of cupping.' (Muwatta of Imam Malik, Chapter: Fidyah of one who shaves before sacrificing, number 239) Proof (2): The hadith to establish: from Ibn Bukaynah (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) had cupping performed while he was in ihram.' (Bukhari, Chapter: Cupping for the Muhrim, number 1836; Muslim, Chapter: Permissibility of Cupping for the Muhrim, number 1202)
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage addresses the penalty for shaving the hair at the cupping site on the neck during ihram. The matn states the ruling and then provides two proofs. Abu Hanifa holds that one must sacrifice a sheep (dam), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider charity (sadaqah) sufficient. The first proof is a statement from Imam Malik in the Muwatta, which categorizes many forms of hair removal under fidyah. The second proof is the authentic hadith from Ibn Bukaynah that the Prophet himself had cupping while in ihram. This hadith indicates that cupping is permissible; however, the shaving of the hair at the site incurs a penalty. The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf highlights the difference in the severity of the penalty. The relied-upon view for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa, requiring a blood sacrifice.

Key Terms
محاجم (mahājim): Places where cupping (hijama) is performed, typically on the neck or back.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice, specifically a sheep or goat, required as a penalty for certain ihram violations.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity, here referring to giving half a sa' of wheat or its equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A blood sacrifice (dam)
B) Charity (sadaqah)
C) Fasting three days
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Shaving the cupping site in ihram incurs a wajib penalty; Abu Hanifa's view requiring a blood sacrifice is the relied-upon position.

Cutting Nails During Ihram
Ruling on penalty for cutting nails with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi penalties for cutting nails during ihram and distinguish between the positions of the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Cutting five or more nails from one limb requires dam; fewer or scattered requires sadaqah.

In this passage, the author details the penalties for cutting nails while in ihram, distinguishing between different quantities and distributions. The ruling is not uniform: it depends on how many nails are cut and whether they come from the same limb. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) present a nuanced scale, while Imam Muhammad in another transmission holds a stricter view. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the hajj penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The subject is cutting nails (azfar) during ihram. Determine the legal category: penalty for violating ihram restrictions.
Ihram violations require compensation (dam or sadaqah).
2
Parse the four scenarios
The text describes: (1) cutting all nails of hands and feet → dam; (2) cutting one hand or foot → dam; (3) cutting fewer than five nails → sadaqah; (4) cutting five scattered nails from hands and feet → sadaqah.
Scattered means not all on one limb.
3
Identify the ruling for each scenario
Note the hukm (penalty) attached to each scenario: dam for full limb or more, sadaqah for less.
The threshold is five nails on one limb.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The position described above is attributed to 'huma' (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Then Muhammad is reported to have said dam for any cutting, regardless of quantity.
This is a difference within the Hanafi school.
5
Recognize the proofs cited
The text cites a statement from Malik in the Muwatta prohibiting nail-cutting, and a statement from Hasan and Ata' that trimming a broken nail before it breaks requires blood.
These are the dalil for the general rule and the specific penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ قَصَّ أَظافِيرَ يَدَيْهِ وَرِجْلَيْهِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ. وَإِنْ قَصَّ يَدًا أَوْ رِجْلًا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ. وَإِنْ قَصَّ أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسَةِ أَظافِيرَ فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ. وَإِنْ قَصَّ خَمْسَةَ أَظافِيرَ مُتَفَرِّقَةٍ مِنْ يَدَيْهِ وَرِجْلَيْهِ فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ. وَهَذَا عِنْدَهُمَا. وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ عَلَيْهِ الدَّمُ.

وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت ... قَالَ مَالِكٌ: «لَا يَصْلُحُ لِلْمُحْرِمِ أَنْ يَنْتِفَ مِنْ شَعَرِهِ شَيْئًا، وَلَا يَحْلِقَهُ، وَلَا يُقَصِرَهُ، حَتَّى يَحِلَّ إِلَّا أَنْ يُصِيبَهُ أَذًى فِي رَأْسِهِ. فَعَلَيْهِ فِدْيَةٌ. كَمَا أَمَرَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى وَلَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُ أَنْ يُقَلَّمَ أَظْفَارَهُ، وَلَا يَقْتُلَ قَمْلَةً. (الموطأ)

وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت ... عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، وَعَطَاءٍ، قَالَ: «إِذَا انْكَسَرَ ظُفُرُهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الكَسَرَ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ شَيْءٌ، فَإِنْ قَلَّمَهُ مِنْ قَبْلِ أَنْ يَنْكَسِرَ، فَعَلَيْهِ دم» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة)
And if he cuts the nails of his hands and feet, then upon him is a blood sacrifice. And if he cuts one hand or foot, then upon him is a blood sacrifice. And if he cuts fewer than five nails, then upon him is charity. And if he cuts five scattered nails from his hands and feet, then upon him is charity. And this is according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. And Muhammad said: upon him is the blood sacrifice. Proof (1): The saying of the follower: Malik said: 'It is not proper for the muhrim to pluck any of his hair, nor shave it, nor trim it until he becomes halal, except if he suffers an ailment on his head. (Muwatta) Proof (1): The saying of the follower from al-Hasan and Ata': 'When his nail is broken from where it broke, nothing is upon him; but if he trims it before it breaks, upon him is blood.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah)

Commentary
This passage details the penalties for cutting nails during ihram. The main ruling distinguishes between cutting all nails (blood sacrifice), cutting a whole hand/foot (blood sacrifice), cutting fewer than five nails (charity), and cutting five scattered nails (charity) — this is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. However, Imam Muhammad (in another transmission) holds that any nail-cutting requires a blood sacrifice. The proofs are from Imam Malik's general prohibition of nail-cutting and from the statement of Hasan and Ata' that trimming a broken nail before it breaks requires blood. This shows that the penalty depends on the quantity of nails cut. The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn for the distinctions, but some Hanafi authorities follow Muhammad's stricter view.

متفرقة (mutafarriqah): Scattered, not from the same hand or foot.

Fidyah for Ihram Violations Due to Excuse
Ruling on fidyah for excused ihram violations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options of fidyah for a muhrim who violates ihram due to a valid excuse, identify the Quranic and hadith proofs, and apply the ruling to similar cases of necessity.

Core Idea
When a muhrim acts out of necessity, fidyah offers a choice: sacrifice, charity, or fasting.

During ihram, certain acts are prohibited. But when a genuine excuse arises—such as illness or infestation—the Shari'ah provides relief. This lesson explains the fidyah (compensation) required and the options available, based on clear Quranic and Prophetic evidence. Understanding this balances the sanctity of ihram with human need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and the ruling
The passage mentions three prohibited acts (applying perfume, wearing sewn clothes, shaving) performed due to an excuse. The ruling is that fidyah becomes wajib, and the person has a choice.
Note the phrase 'min 'udhrin' – due to an excuse – which is the key condition.
2
Read the three options of fidyah
The text lists: slaughter a sheep, give three sa' of food to six poor people, or fast three days. Memorize these exactly.
These are the only options; no other penalty applies.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse from Al-Baqarah (2:196) is cited. It explicitly mentions fidyah for illness or head ailment. The word 'aw' (or) indicates a choice.
This verse directly supports the three options.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Ka'b ibn Ujrah shows the Prophet giving this same choice when his head was infested with lice. This is a practical application of the verse.
The hadith confirms the ruling and its scope beyond just shaving.
5
Apply the ruling widely
The ruling is not limited to shaving; it generalizes to any ihram violation due to necessity. The Hanafi school applies it to perfume and wearing sewn clothes as well, by analogy.
This is an example of qiyas based on the common illa of necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ تَطَيَّبَ أَوْ لَبِسَ أَوْ حَلَقَ مِنْ عُذْرٍ فَهُوَ مُخَيَّرٌ: إِنْ شَاءَ ذَبَحَ شَاةً وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَصَدَّقَ عَلَى سِتَّةِ مَسَاكِينَ بِثَلَاثَةِ أَصْوُعٍ مِنْ الطَّعَامِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ صَامَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ.

وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت ... {فَمَن كَانَ مِنكُم مَّرِيضًا أَوْ بِهِ أَذًى مِّن رَّأْسِهِ فَفِدْيَةٌ مِّن صِيَامٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ أَوْ نُسُكٍ} [البقرة: 196]

وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت ... عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ عَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ عُجْرَةَ قَالَ: وَقَفَ عَلَيَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِالْحُدَيْبِيَةِ وَرَأْسِي يَتَهَافَتُ قَمْلًا فَقَالَ: «يُؤْذِيكَ هَوَامُّكَ؟» قُلْتُ: نَعَمْ، قَالَ: «احْلِقْ وَصُمْ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ أَوْ تَصَدَّقْ بِفَرَقٍ بَيْنَ سِتَّةٍ أَوِ انْسُكْ بِمَا تَيَسَّرَ» (بخاري: 1815)
And if he applies perfume, or wears [sewn clothes], or shaves due to an excuse, then he has a choice: if he wishes, he may slaughter a sheep; if he wishes, he may give charity to six poor people with three sa' of food; and if he wishes, he may fast three days. Proof (1): The verse to establish: {And if any of you is ill or has an ailment in his scalp, then a compensation of fasting or charity or sacrifice.} [Al-Baqarah 2:196] Proof (2): The hadith to establish: from Ibn Umar from Ka'b ibn Ujrah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stood over me at Hudaybiyyah while my head was infested with lice. He said, ‘Are your pests troubling you?’ I said, ‘Yes.’ He said, ‘Shave and fast three days, or give charity to six [poor people] with a farq [of food], or offer a sacrifice with whatever is available.’ (Bukhari: 1815)
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a muhrim has a valid excuse to apply perfume, wear sewn clothes, or shave. The ruling provides a threefold option: sacrifice a sheep, feed six poor people with three sa' of food, or fast three days. The evidence is the Quranic verse (2:196) which mentions fidyah for illness or head ailment, and the hadith of Ka'b ibn Ujrah where the Prophet gave him this very choice when he had lice. This demonstrates that the fidyah is not a fixed penalty but a choice to suit the person's capability. The Hanafi school uses this as a general rule for all violations due to necessity, not just head shaving.

Key Terms
فدية (fidyah): A compensatory penalty for violating ihram due to a valid excuse, consisting of one of three options.
مخير (mukhayyar): Having a choice with full freedom; all options are equally valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Fast seven days

Key Takeaway
Fidyah for ihram violations due to excuse is a three-option compensatory mechanism, not a fixed penalty.

Kissing or Touching with Desire During Ihram (Penalty: Dam)
Ruling on penalty for kissing or touching with desire while in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kissing or touching with desire during ihram and identify its proof from a Companion statement.

Core Idea
Kissing with desire in ihram demands dam — a wajib penalty for passion before pilgrimage.

This lesson addresses a specific ihram violation: kissing or touching one's spouse with sexual desire. While intercourse is the greatest violation, even lesser acts of desire incur a wajib penalty. We will examine the ruling, its proof from a Companion's statement, and why the Hanafi school holds it as wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that if a muhrim kisses or touches with desire, upon him is a blood sacrifice (dam).
The act includes both kissing (qabla) and touching (lams) when done with desire.
2
Recognize the proof type
The author cites a Companion's statement (qawl al-sahabi) as the evidence.
In Hanafi usul, a Companion's statement is a valid proof when it does not contradict other evidence.
3
Locate the dalil
The dalil is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'Whoever kisses his wife while in ihram, let him shed blood.'
The exact source references are provided in the text.
4
Apply Hanafi usul principle
The command 'فليهرق دما' (let him shed blood) is an imperative, which indicates wujub according to the Hanafi principle that al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
This principle makes the dam wajib, not merely recommended.
5
Note the effect and conditions
The ruling applies only when desire is present; without desire, no penalty. The dam is wajib and must be fulfilled.
This is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قَبَّلَ أَوْ لَمَسَ بِشَهْوَةٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ

وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت ... عَنْ أَبِي جَعْفَرٍ عَنْ عَلِقٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ, قَالَ : " مَنْ قَبَّلَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ فَلْيُهْرِقُ دَمًا (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي: 9790; مصنف ابن شيبة: 12821)
So if he kisses or touches with desire, then upon him is a blood sacrifice. Proof (1): The saying of the Companion: from Abu Ja'far from 'Alqamah (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'Whoever kisses his wife while in ihram, let him shed blood.' (Sunan al-Kubra of al-Bayhaqi: 9790; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: 12821)
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This ruling addresses a muhrim who kisses or touches his spouse with sexual desire. The penalty is a blood sacrifice (dam). The proof is the statement of the Companion 'Alqamah (or Ali according to other narrations) that such an act requires shedding blood. This is a established ruling in the Hanafi school for acts that are less than intercourse but involve desire. The blood sacrifice is wajib, not merely recommended.

Key Terms
بشهوة (bi-shahwah): With sexual desire, as opposed to casual or non-sexual touch.
لمس (lams): Touching, specifically with the hand or body, with intention of desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Blood sacrifice (dam)
B) Charity (sadaqah)
C) Nothing
D) Fasting three days

Key Takeaway
Kissing or touching with desire during ihram necessitates a blood sacrifice (dam) according to the Hanafi school, based on the Companion's statement.

Intercourse Before Arafah Invalidates Hajj
Ruling on intercourse before Arafah and its consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sexual intercourse before Arafah and explain the required penalties.

Core Idea
Intercourse before Arafah invalidates hajj but you must continue; sacrifice a sheep and repeat next year.

This lesson addresses one of the most severe ihram violations: sexual intercourse before the essential standing at Arafah. The Hanafi school outlines clear consequences that balance the gravity of the sin with the obligation to complete the pilgrimage rites. We will examine the ruling, its textual proof, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Whoever engages in sexual intercourse (front or back) intentionally or forgetfully before standing at Arafah – his hajj is invalid (fasid).
The term 'fasid' means the hajj is legally invalid but must be completed, unlike 'batil' which is void entirely.
2
List the Three Consequences
1) He must continue the remaining rites as if valid. 2) He must sacrifice a sheep. 3) He must perform hajj again the following year.
The text says 'يمضي في الحج كما يمضي من لم يفسد حجه' – he proceeds as one whose hajj is not invalid.
3
Examine the Proof
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas indicating that missing Arafah invalidates hajj and requires repetition. Intercourse before Arafah is analogized to missing Arafah because both cause the hajj to be incomplete.
The second hadith from Ka'b ibn Ujrah is likely mismatched due to OCR; it deals with fidyah for shaving, not intercourse.
4
Understand the Analogy (Qiyas)
The Hanafi school uses qiyas: missing Arafah (invalidates hajj + requires repetition) is the asl; intercourse before Arafah is the far' because both render the hajj incomplete before the essential stop.
The illa (effective cause) is 'rendering the hajj incomplete before Arafah'.
5
Note the Hanafi Terminology: Fasid vs Batil
Fasid means the act is flawed but still requires completion; batil means void with no obligation to continue. Here, hajj is fasid, not batil.
This distinction affects whether the pilgrim must continue (fasid) or can abandon (batil).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ جَامَعَ فِي أَحَدِ السَّبِيلَيْنِ عَامِدًا أَوْ نَاسِيًا قَبْلَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ فَسَدَ حَجُّهُ وَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ وَيَمْضِي فِي الْحَجِّ كَمَا يَمْضِي مَنْ لَمْ يَفْسُدْ حَجُّهُ وَعَلَيْهِ الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِلِ.

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت ... عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ, قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ أَدْرَكَ عَرَفَاتٍ فَوَقَفَ بِمَا وَالْمُزْدَلِفَةَ فَقَدْ ثُمَّ حَجَّهُ وَمَنْ فَاتَهُ عَرَفَاتٌ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ فَلْيَحِلَّ بِعُمْرَةٍ وَعَلَيْهِ الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِلِ» (السنن الدار قطني: 2519)

وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت ... عَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ عُجْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ رَآهُ وَأَنَّهُ يَسْقُطُ عَلَى وَجْهِهِ. . . أَوْ يُهْدِيَ شَاةً، أَوْ يَصُومَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ (بخاري: 1817)
Whoever has sexual intercourse in one of the two passages [front or back] intentionally or forgetfully before standing at Arafah, his hajj is invalid, and upon him is a sheep, and he continues in the hajj as one whose hajj is not invalid proceeds, and upon him is the hajj next year. Proof (1): The hadith to establish: from Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever reaches Arafat and stands there and at Muzdalifah, then his hajj is [complete], and whoever misses Arafat has missed the hajj; let him make it an umrah and upon him is the hajj next year.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni: 2519) Proof (2): The hadith to establish: from Ka'b ibn Ujrah that the Messenger of Allah saw him and that he was falling on his face... or sacrifice a sheep, or fast three days. (Bukhari: 1817)
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage addresses the most severe ihram violation: sexual intercourse before the critical stop at Arafah. The ruling is that the hajj becomes invalid (fasid), but the person must continue the remaining rites as usual, not abandon them. Afterward, he must sacrifice a sheep and also perform the hajj again the following year. The two proofs are: first, the hadith of Ibn Abbas that emphasizes the centrality of Arafah; missing it invalidates the hajj. However, the hadith is about missing Arafah entirely, not specifically about intercourse. The second hadith from Ka'b ibn Ujrah seems out of place as it is about fidyah for head ailment; this may be a OCR mixing. Nonetheless, the Hanafi ruling is clear: intercourse before Arafah necessitates a sheep sacrifice and repetition of hajj next year.

Key Terms
السبيلين (al-sabīlayn): The two passages: front (genital) and back (anal), meaning sexual intercourse.
فسد حجه (fasada hajjuhu): His hajj becomes invalid (fasid), requiring repetition, but the rites must be completed.
من قابل (min qābil): The following year; one year later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the consequences of sexual intercourse before Arafah while in ihram according to the Hanafi school?
A) Hajj becomes invalid (fasid), continue rites, sacrifice a sheep, repeat hajj next year
B) Hajj becomes batil, abandon rites, sacrifice a camel
C) Hajj remains valid but requires fasting three days
D) Hajj becomes invalid, perform umrah instead, no need to repeat

Key Takeaway
Sexual intercourse before Arafah invalidates the hajj (fasid) and incurs three penalties: continue rites, sacrifice a sheep, and repeat hajj the following year.

Kissing with Desire in Ihram: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof from a Companion's statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for kissing or touching with desire during ihram, identify the proof from a Companion's statement, and explain why the expiation is a dam.

Core Idea
Kissing with desire in ihram requires a wajib dam — a Companion's statement provides the proof.

In this lesson, we examine a specific violation of ihram: kissing or touching one's spouse with desire. The text from Al-Quduri presents the ruling and its basis in a statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib (رضي الله عنه). Understanding this ruling requires familiarity with the Hanafi classification of violations and the use of Companion statements as evidence. We will also note the condition 'with desire' and its legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The text states: 'If he kisses or touches with desire, then upon him is a dam.' Identify the act (kissing or touching with desire) and the ruling (wajib: a dam must be offered).
The term 'dam' refers to sacrificing a sheep or goat.
2
Locate the proof
The text cites a statement from Ali (رضي الله عنه): 'Whoever kisses his wife while in ihram, let him spill blood (sacrifice).' This is a qawl al-sahabi (Companion statement).
The chain is from Abu Ja'far from Ali.
3
Analyse the proof
In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'فَلْيُهْرِقْ' indicates obligation (wujub). Thus, the ruling is wajib, not simply recommended.
The imperative form is taken as a default for obligation unless there is a qarinah to the contrary.
4
Note the condition of desire
The text explicitly adds 'بِشَهْوَةٍ' (with desire). Without desire, the ruling does not apply. This distinction is crucial.
The Shafi'i school also distinguishes based on desire, but some differences exist in other aspects.
5
Identify the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position is that any lustful kissing/touching requires a dam. The Shafi'i school agrees on the ruling for kissing with desire but differs on whether touching without desire requires anything.
The practical difference: in Shafi'i, touching without desire may incur no penalty, while Hanafi may extend the ruling by analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قَبَّلَ أَوْ لَمَسَ بِشَهْوَةٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ. وَجْهُهُ: قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِهِ عَنْ أَبِي جَعْفَرٍ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: "مَنْ قَبَّلَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ فَلْيُهْرِقْ دَمًا".
If he kisses or touches with desire, then upon him is a dam. Its proof: the statement of the companion for its establishment: from Abu Ja'far from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'Whoever kisses his wife while in ihram, let him spill blood (i.e., sacrifice an animal).'
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The ruling states that a person in the state of ihram who kisses or touches his/her spouse with sexual desire must offer a dam (a sheep or goat) as expiation. The proof is a statement of the companion Ali (رضي الله عنه), which is a form of dalil (evidence) for the Hanafi school. The act of kissing or touching with desire is considered a minor violation of ihram, not as severe as intercourse, hence the penalty is a dam rather than a badanah (camel/cow) or a shah. The proof is a qawl al-sahabi, which is a source of law in the Hanafi school when not contradicted by Quran or Sunnah.

Key Terms
دَم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as expiation for certain violations of ihram.
مُحْرِم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A badanah (camel/cow)
B) A dam (sheep/goat)
C) Fasting three days
D) Nothing is required

Key Takeaway
Kissing or touching with desire during ihram requires a dam, proven by a Companion's statement and the Hanafi principle that an imperative indicates obligation.

Rulings on Intercourse in Hajj and Umrah
Lists rulings for jima' at different stages of Hajj/Umrah with their consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for intercourse at different stages of Hajj and Umrah, and explain why the ritual's validity depends on the stage.

Core Idea
Intercourse in Hajj or Umrah may or may not invalidate the ritual — the stage determines the ruling.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents the nuanced Hanafi position on intercourse (jima') during Hajj and Umrah. It clarifies that the same act can have dramatically different consequences depending on when it occurs: after Wuquf, after halq, or at different points in Umrah tawaf. The rulings are built on the principle that once the primary pillar (wuquf in Hajj, four circuits in Umrah) is completed, the ritual cannot be undone by subsequent violations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ritual
Determine whether it is Hajj or Umrah, and the stage at which intercourse occurs.
2
Apply the ruling based on timing
For each stage, state whether the ritual is invalidated or remains valid, and what penalty (badanah or shaat) is required.
3
Trace the principle behind the ruling
The key factor is whether the essential pillar (wuquf for Hajj, four circuits for Umrah) has been completed. If yes, the ritual stands; if no, it is invalidated.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school disagrees with Shafi'i on the effect of intercourse after Wuquf; explain the dispute and its practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْحِنَايَاتِ فِي الْحَجّ ال وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُفَارِقَ امْرَأَتَهُ إِذَا حَجَّ بِمَا فِي الْقَضَاءِ ١٢ وَإِنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ لَمَّ يَفْسُدْ حَجُّهُ وَعَلَيْهِ بَدَنَةٌ ٣ وَإِنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْخَلْقِ فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ وَمَنْ جَامَعَ فِي الْعُمْرَةِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَطُوفَ لَهَا أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ أَفْسَدَهَا وَمَضَى فِيهَا وَقَضَاهَا وَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ وَإِنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَمَا طَافَ هَا أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ وَمَنْ جَامَعَ نَاسِيًا كَمَنْ جَامَعَ عَامِدًا
Chapter of violations in Hajj. And it is not required that he separate from his wife when he performs the makeup Hajj. And if he has intercourse after standing at Arafah, his Hajj is not invalidated, and upon him is a camel. And if he has intercourse after shaving, upon him is a sheep. And whoever has intercourse in Umrah before he circumambulates four circuits, he invalidates it, and he continues in it and makes it up, and upon him is a sheep. And if he has intercourse after he has circumambulated four circuits, upon him is a sheep. And whoever has intercourse forgetfully is like one who has intercourse intentionally.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (ahkam) from the chapter on violations (jinayat) in Hajj, specifically regarding intercourse (jima'). The text first addresses the makeup Hajj: a person who invalidated his Hajj and must repeat it is not required to separate from his wife during the makeup journey. Then it differentiates based on timing. Intercourse after Wuquf at Arafah does not invalidate the Hajj (since the essential standing has been completed), but a camel (badanah) is due as penalty. After the first tahallul (shaving), only a sheep is required. For Umrah, if intercourse occurs before completing four circuits of tawaf, the Umrah is invalidated; one must continue, then repeat it, and sacrifice a sheep. If after four circuits, the Umrah remains valid but a sheep is still obligatory. Finally, forgetfulness does not change the ruling: the penalty applies whether intentional or forgetful. This reflects the Hanafi position that such violations require compensation (dam) but may or may not invalidate the ritual depending on the stage.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A camel (or cow) that is sacrificed as a penalty for certain violations in Hajj.
شاة (shaat): A sheep or goat used as a sacrifice (dam) for lesser violations.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, which is part of the first tahallul in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person has intercourse after standing at Arafah during Hajj?
A) Hajj is invalidated and must be repeated with a camel penalty.
B) Hajj remains valid but a camel is obligatory.
C) Hajj is valid and no penalty is required.
D) Only a sheep is required.

Key Takeaway
The timing of intercourse in Hajj or Umrah determines both the validity of the ritual and the penalty — a single act has multiple possible outcomes.

Penalties for Tawaf without Purity
Prescribes penalties for tawaf with impurity and advises repeating to avoid penalty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required penalty (sadaqah or dam) for each type of tawaf performed in a state of minor or major impurity, and explain the Hanafi position that the tawaf remains valid with a wajib compensation.

Core Idea
Tawaf without purity is valid but deficient; a wajib penalty compensates the deficiency.

This passage from al-Quduri outlines the Hanafi view on tawaf performed without ritual purity. It details specific penalties for tawaf al-qudum, al-ziyarah, and al-sadar, distinguishing between minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janabah). The core principle is that purity is highly recommended for tawaf, but its absence does not invalidate the act; instead, a wajib compensation is due, and it is better to repeat the tawaf while in Makkah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three tawafs and their penalties
List the three types of tawaf mentioned: qudum (arrival), ziyarah (visitation), sadar (departure). For each, note the penalty for minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janabah).
Penalty scale: sadaqah (charity of half a sa') < sheep < camel (badanah).
2
Understand the default: repeating the tawaf is better
The text says it is afdal (better) to repeat the tawaf while in Makkah, and then no slaughter is required. This shows the penalty is a removable deficiency.
Repeating removes the deficiency, so the penalty becomes unnecessary.
3
Link to the dalil: tawaf is like prayer
Recall the hadith: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you speak in it.' This establishes that purity is a condition for perfection, but not for validity in the Hanafi school (unlike prayer).
Hanafi usul: the command for purity in tawaf is understood as recommended (nadb) for validity, but omission requires compensation.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school holds purity as a condition for validity; tawaf without wudu is invalid and must be repeated without any penalty option.
This difference arises from how each school interprets the hadith's analogy.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a specific case (e.g., a pilgrim performs tawaf al-ziyarah in janabah), determine the penalty (camel) and the option to repeat.
If repeated while in Makkah, no penalty; if not, the camel is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ مُحْدِثًا فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ جُنُبًا فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ وَمَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الزِيَارَةِ مُحْدِثًا فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ جُنُبًا فَعَلَيْهِ بَدَنَةٌ وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يُعِيدَ الطَّوَافَ مَا دَامَ بِمَكَّةَ وَلَا ذَبْحَ عَلَيْهِ وَمَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الصَّدَرِ مُحْدِنَا فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ جُنُبًا فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ
And whoever circumambulates the tawaf of arrival while in a state of minor impurity, upon him is charity. And if he is in major impurity (janabah), upon him is a sheep. And whoever circumambulates the tawaf of visitation (ziyarah) while in minor impurity, upon him is a sheep. And if he is in major impurity, upon him is a camel. And it is better that he repeat the tawaf as long as he is in Makkah, and no slaughter is upon him. And whoever circumambulates the tawaf of departure (sadar) while in minor impurity, upon him is charity. And if he is in major impurity, upon him is a sheep.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on tawaf performed without ritual purity. It distinguishes between three types of tawaf: tawaf al-qudum (arrival), tawaf al-ziyarah (visitation, the essential one), and tawaf al-sadar (farewell). For each, the penalty differs based on whether the impurity is minor (hadath) or major (janabah). For tawaf al-qudum: minor impurity requires sadaqah (charity, equivalent to half a sa' of wheat or similar), major impurity requires a sheep. For tawaf al-ziyarah: minor impurity requires a sheep, major impurity requires a camel (badanah). For tawaf al-sadar: minor impurity requires sadaqah, major impurity requires a sheep. Importantly, the text notes that it is better (afdal) to repeat the tawaf while still in Makkah, and then no penalty is due. This is because the penalty is for the deficiency, and repeating the act removes that deficiency. This ruling is based on the analogy of tawaf to prayer, and the evidence that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) said: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you speak in it.' (Tirmidhi 960).

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Minor ritual impurity that requires wudu, such as passing wind or urine.
جنب (junub): Major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, due to sexual intercourse or seminal emission.
صدقة (sadaqah): A charitable gift of half a sa' of wheat or equivalent, as a penalty for minor impurity during tawaf al-qudum/sadar.
شاة (shaat): A sheep, used as a penalty (dam) for certain types of tawaf with impurity.
بدنة (badanah): A camel, the penalty for tawaf al-ziyarah performed in janabah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the penalty for a person who performs tawaf al-ziyarah in a state of janabah?
A) Sadaqah
B) A sheep
C) A camel
D) No penalty if repeated

Key Takeaway
Tawaf performed without ritual purity is valid in the Hanafi school, but a wajib penalty (sadaqah, sheep, or camel) must be given unless the tawaf is repeated while in Makkah.

Ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum with Impurity and Its Compensation
States penalty for Tawaf al-Qudum in impurity and preference to repeat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for Tawaf al-Qudum performed in impurity, differentiate the penalties for hadath and janabah, and explain why repeating the tawaf is preferable.

Core Idea
Tawaf is like prayer in requiring purity, but its deficiency is compensated by penalty rather than invalidation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on Tawaf al-Qudum when performed without ritual purity. While the act remains valid, it incurs a specific penalty—sadaqah for minor impurity and a sheep for major impurity. The text also emphasizes that repeating the tawaf correctly removes the need for any penalty, making it the preferred course of action.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and penalties
The text gives two categories: minor impurity (hadath) incurs sadaqah; major impurity (janabah) incurs a sheep (shah). The phrase 'فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ' may be a copyist error; the intended meaning is that for janabah, a sheep is due, and for hadath, sadaqah.
Note the distinction: the penalty increases with the severity of impurity.
2
Identify the preferable action (afdal)
Repeating the tawaf correctly while in Makkah removes the deficiency, canceling the penalty. The text states 'الْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يُعِيدَ الطَّوَافَ' – it is better to repeat.
Repeating is not obligatory but recommended; if one does not repeat, the penalty stands.
3
Analyze the proofs provided
Three proofs are cited: (1) the hadith equating tawaf to prayer (Tirmidhi, Nasa'i), (2) the hadith of Aisha (Bukhari) ordering her to delay tawaf until purity, and (3) the Quranic verse commanding tawaf. For janabah, a statement of Ibn Abbas is added.
The comparison to prayer is not absolute because speech is allowed; thus tawaf is valid but deficient without purity.
4
Understand the Hanafi usul behind the ruling
Hanafis hold that tawaf without purity is valid but deficient, unlike prayer which is invalid. The penalty compensates for the deficiency. This is based on the principle that the requirement of purity for tawaf is a condition of perfection, not validity.
This distinguishes Hanafi ruling from other schools that consider purity a condition of validity.

بَابُ الْحِنَايَاتِ فِي الْحَجّ وَمَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ مُحْدِثًا فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَإِنْ كَانَ جُنُبًا فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يُعِيدَ الطَّوَافَ مَا دَامَ بِمَكَّةَ وَلَا ذَبْحَ عَلَيْهِ. وَجْهُ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ مُحْدِثًا فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «الطَّوَافُ حَوْلَ البَيْتِ مِثْلُ الصَّلَاةِ، إِلَّا أَنَّكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ فِيهِ، فَمَنْ تَكَلَّمَ فِيهِ فَلَا يَتَكَلَّمَنَّ إِلَّا بِخَيْرٍ» (الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الكَلَامِ فِي الطَّوَافِ، نمبر: 960/ سنن النسائي: إِبَاحَةُ الْكَلَامِ فِي الطَّوَافِ، نمبر: 2922). وَجْهُ (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الْقُدُومِ مُحْدِثًا فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ فِي أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: «قَدِمْتُ مَكَّةَ وَأَنَا حَائِضٌ وَلَمْ أَطْفْ بِالْبَيْتِ، وَلَا بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ، قَالَتْ: فَشَكَوْتُ ذَلِكَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: افْعَلِي كَمَا يَفْعَلُ الْحَاجُ غَيْرَ أَنْ لَا تَطُوفِي بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَطْهُرِي.» (بخاري بَابٌ : تَقْضِي الْخَائِضُ الْمَنَاسِكَ كُلَّهَا إِلَّا الطَّوَافَ غبر : 1650). وَجْهٌ (3) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الْقَدُومِ مُحْدِثًا فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ ثُمَّ لْيَقْضُوا تَفَتَهُمْ وَلْيُوفُوا نُذُورَهُمْ وَلْيَطَّوَّفُواْ بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ ﴾ (القرآن: سورة الحج، 22 ألاية نمبر: 29). وَجْهٌ (1) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ كَانَ جُنُبًا فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «مَنْ نَسِيَ شَيْئًا مِنْ نُسُكِهِ أَوْ تَرَكَهُ فَلْيُهْرِقُ دَمًا» (سنن الدارقطني: كِتَاب الحج،: 2534). أُصُولٌ: أَفْضَلُ هُوَ أَنْ يَعِيدَ الطَّوَافَ بِحَالَتِ جَنَابَةٍ أَوْ حَدَثٍ وَإِذَا لَمْ يَأْتِ بِهِ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ صَدَقَةٌ أَوْ بَدَنَةٌ، لِأَنَّ النَّقْصَ الَّذِي وَجَبَ بِسَبَبِهِ ذَلِكَ قَدْ زَالَ.
Chapter of penalties in Hajj. Whoever performs Tawaf al-Qudum while in a state of minor impurity must give sadaqah, and if he is in a state of major impurity, he must give a sheep, then sadaqah. And the better practice is that he repeats the tawaf as long as he is in Makkah, and no slaughter is upon him. Proof 1: The hadith for establishing that whoever performs Tawaf al-Qudum while impure must give sadaqah: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The circumambulation around the House is like prayer, except that you speak in it. So whoever speaks in it, let him speak nothing but good.' (Tirmidhi and Nasa'i). Proof 2: The hadith for establishing that whoever performs Tawaf al-Qudum while impure must give sadaqah: from Aisha that she said: 'I arrived in Makkah while menstruating and did not circumambulate the House nor between Safa and Marwa. She said: I complained about that to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). He said: Do as the pilgrim does except that do not circumambulate the House until you become pure.' (Bukhari). Proof 3: The verse for establishing that whoever performs Tawaf al-Qudum while impure must give sadaqah: 'Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and circumambulate the Ancient House' (Quran 22:29). Proof 1 (for the janabah ruling): The statement of a Companion for establishing that if he is in major impurity he must give a sheep, then sadaqah: from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him spill blood.' (Darqutni). Principles: It is better that he repeat the tawaf if it was done in a state of major or minor impurity, and if he does not repeat it, no sadaqah or camel is necessary, because the deficiency that necessitated that has been removed.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn presents the ruling for Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival circumambulation) performed without ritual purity. The text distinguishes between minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janabah). For hadath, the penalty is sadaqah (charity, which in this context is interpreted as a specific amount, often half a sa' of wheat or similar). For janabah, the penalty is a sheep (shah). The text then adds that it is better (afdal) to repeat the tawaf while still in Makkah, and if one repeats, no additional sacrifice is required. This is because the original deficiency is removed by the correct performance. The author then provides proofs: (1) a hadith equating tawaf to prayer in its requirement of purity, though speech is allowed; (2) the hadith of Aisha showing that tawaf requires purity; (3) the Quranic verse commanding tawaf after completing rites, implying it is a pillar; and (4) the general principle from Ibn Abbas that anyone who omits a rite must offer a blood sacrifice. The commentary (usul) clarifies that the better view is to repeat, and if not repeated, the penalty stands.

Key Terms
الْحِنَايَات (al-jinayat): Penalties, violations, or crimes that require expiation or compensation in Hajj.
طَوَاف الْقُدُوم (tawaf al-qudum): The circumambulation of the Kaaba performed upon arrival in Makkah, considered sunnah mu'akkadah.
صَدَقَة (sadaqah): In this context, a specific amount of charity given as penalty for a deficiency in tawaf, equivalent to half a sa' of wheat or its value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on Tawaf al-Qudum performed in a state of minor impurity (hadath)?
A) Invalid, must be repeated.
B) Valid, no penalty.
C) Valid, but a sheep must be sacrificed.
D) Valid, but sadaqah must be given.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf performed in impurity is valid in the Hanafi school, but it incurs a penalty; repeating it correctly removes the deficiency.

Expiation for Leaving Three or Fewer Circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Ruling with proof from a companion's saying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the expiation required for leaving three or fewer circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and explain the proof from the companion's saying.

Core Idea
Leaving 1-3 circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah requires a sheep; the companion's saying proves wujub of sacrifice.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri regarding a pilgrim who omits part of the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The text specifies the expiation (shaat) for leaving up to three circuits, and supports it with a proof from Ibn Abbas. This illustrates how Hanafi fiqh uses a companion's statement as evidence for wajib expiations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is omitting three or fewer circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling is that a sheep (shaat) must be sacrificed.
The ruling is clear and unconditional for the range of 1-3 circuits.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him spill blood.' This is a companion's saying (qawl al-sahabi).
In Hanafi usul, qawl al-sahabi is authoritative when no contrary opinion exists.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فَلْيُهْرِقْ دَمًا' (let him spill blood) indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi principles: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
The expiation is thus wajib, not just recommended.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies to any omission of up to three circuits. If four or more are left, the ruling differs (remaining in ihram).
The text only covers up to three; the complementary rule is known from other sources.
5
Evaluate the authority
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position. The proof is zanni al-thubut (companion's saying) and zanni al-dalalah (imperative), but sufficient for wujub in Hanafi usul.
Other schools may classify Tawaf al-Ziyarah differently, affecting the expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ مِنْ طَوَافِ الزِيَارَةِ فَمَا دُونَهَا فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ 19 وجه:(۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ تَرَكَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ مِنْ طَوَافِ الزِّيَارَةِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «مَنْ نَسِيَ شَيْئًا مِنْ نُسُكِهِ أَوْ تَرَكَهُ فَلْيُهْرِقْ دَمًا» . (سنن الدار قطني: كِتَابُ الحَجّ، نمبر: 2534/ المؤطا لإمام مالك: بَابُ مَا يَفْعَلُ مَنْ نَسِيَ مِنْ نُسُكِهِ شَيْئًا، نمبر: 240/ سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ مَنْ تَرَكَ شَيْئًا مِنَ الرَّمْيِ حَتَّى يَذْهَبَ أَيَّامُ مِنِّي، نمبر: 9688)
And whoever leaves three circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah or less, upon him is a sheep. 19 Evidence (1): The saying of a companion as proof for 'Whoever leaves three circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah': from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him spill blood.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Hajj, no. 2534; Muwatta Imam Malik, Chapter on what to do for one who forgets something of his rites, no. 240; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on one who leaves some of the throwing until the days of Mina pass, no. 9688)
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri on the expiation for leaving part of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling states that if a pilgrim omits three circuits or fewer, he must slaughter a sheep (shaat). The proof cited is the statement of Ibn Abbas (a companion) that anyone who forgets or leaves any rite must offer a sacrifice. This companion's saying (qawl al-sahabi) is considered authoritative in Hanafi usul. Note that the ruling distinguishes between three or fewer (sheep) and four or more (remaining in ihram).

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory Tawaf after standing at Arafah on the day of Eid, also known as Tawaf al-Ifadah.
شاة (shaat): A sheep or goat, the minimum expiation for certain Hajj omissions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the expiation for a pilgrim who leaves two circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah?
A) A sheep (shaat)
B) Sadaqah
C) Nothing
D) A camel

Key Takeaway
Leaving 1-3 circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah requires a sheep as wajib expiation, based on the companion's saying.

Perpetual Ihram for Missing Majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Ruling on leaving four or more circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a pilgrim who leaves four or more circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and explain the proof cited from the Madinan jurists.

Core Idea
Missing four or more circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah means you stay in ihram forever until you complete them.

This lesson examines a critical rule in Hajj: what happens when a pilgrim omits a significant portion of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The Hanafi school prescribes a severe consequence—perpetual ihram—based on the practice of the Madinan jurists. Understanding this ruling highlights the importance of Tawaf and the school's reliance on transmitted precedents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaving four or more circuits (ashwaṭ) of Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling: the pilgrim remains in the state of ihram indefinitely (muhriman abadan) until those circuits are performed.
The threshold of four circuits constitutes the majority (akthar) of the seven circuits.
2
Recognize the threshold
Leaving three or fewer circuits does not trigger perpetual ihram; only four or more does. This is based on the principle that the majority has the ruling of the whole.
The Hanafi school treats missing the majority as equivalent to missing the entire Tawaf.
3
Trace the dalil
The proof is a saying of the Madinan jurists (qawl al-tabi'ī) transmitted by Ibn Abī al-Zinād: one who forgets Ifadah (Tawaf al-Ifadah) until returning home remains in ihram until he returns and performs Tawaf; if he had intercourse, he must sacrifice a camel. This is analogically extended to missing the majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
The narration is from Sunan al-Bayhaqī (no. 9650) and is considered zannī al-thubūt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ تَرَكَ مِنْهُ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ فَصَاعِدًا بَقِيَ مُحْرِمًا أَبَدًا حَتَّى يَطُوفَهَا ۲۰ وجه: (1)قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِنْ تَرَكَ مِنْهُ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ فَصَاعِدًا حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَنْ أَبِيهِ, عَنِ الْفُقَهَاءِ الَّذِينَ يُنْتَهَى إِلَى قَوْلِهِمْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ كَانُوا يَقُولُونَ : مَنْ نَسِيَ أَنْ يُفِيضَ حَتَّى رَجَعَ إِلَى بِلَادِهِ فَهُوَ حَرَامٌ حِينَ يَذْكُرُ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ فَيَطُوفَ بِهِ فَإِنْ أَصَابَ النِّسَاءَ أَهْدَى بَدَنَةً (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ التَّحَلُّلِ بِالطَّوَافِ إِذَا كَانَ قَدْ سَعَى عَقِيبَ طَوَافِ الْقُدُومِ،: 9650)
And if he leaves from it four circuits or more, he remains in ihram forever until he performs them. 20 Evidence (1): The saying of a follower (tabi'i) as proof for 'And if he leaves from it four circuits or more': Ibn Abi al-Zinad narrated from his father, from the jurists whose words are followed among the people of Madinah, they used to say: 'Whoever forgets to do Ifadah until he returns to his land, he is in a state of prohibition (haram) when he remembers, until he returns to the House and performs Tawaf around it, and if he had intercourse with women, he should sacrifice a camel.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on tahlul by Tawaf if one has done Sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum, no. 9650)
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This ruling states that if a pilgrim omits four circuits or more of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, his ihram does not end; he remains in the state of ihram indefinitely until he completes that Tawaf. This is a severe consequence because the essential part of the Tawaf (the majority) has been missed. The proof cited is the saying of the Madinan jurists, transmitted by Ibn Abi al-Zinad, which deals with a similar case: one who forgets Ifadah (i.e., Tawaf al-Ifadah) until he returns home remains in ihram until he returns and performs Tawaf; if he has had intercourse, he must sacrifice a camel. This supports the Hanafi position that missing the majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah prolongs ihram.

Key Terms
مُحْرِمًا أَبَدًا (muhriman abadan): Remaining in ihram indefinitely until the missing Tawaf is performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a pilgrim who leaves five circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah?
A) He must sacrifice a sheep
B) He remains in ihram until he completes them
C) His Hajj is invalid
D) He must perform Umrah instead

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school imposes perpetual ihram for missing four or more circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, emphasizing the wajib nature of this ritual.
